Resolution of the Shantou Market Strike

Shantou Correspondence: The municipal government levied an additional 20% donation on electricity bills. The General Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the National Government and the Provincial Government to request a temporary suspension of the execution, but the municipal government still implemented the levy, resulting in a city-wide strike that began on the 22nd. At 1:00 PM that afternoon, the General Chamber of Commerce convened the sixth emergency meeting, nominating Chen Jingqing, Ma Zonghan, and Shi Ziqin to meet with Civil Affairs Inspector Huang Zungeng, and nominating Xu Wanru, Li Xiangkun, and Chen Chengwen to meet with Dai Ji, the brigade commander of the 61st Division. Yang Jianping, the Customs Superintendent, and Huang Zungeng, the Civil Affairs Inspector, mediated separately, and a resolution was reached immediately. The General Chamber of Commerce then announced the resumption of business for all stores by gong, and announced the mediation measures to be followed: (1) The request to completely abolish the additional 10-20% donation on electricity bills was agreed upon. It was stipulated that Yang and Huang would negotiate the abolition, and before the resolution, the municipal government could not collect it from the citizens and Yang and Huang would be responsible for the thorough abolition. (2) The request to punish the collection officers and district heads for illegal activities was agreed upon. It was stipulated that Yang and Huang would be responsible for requesting the municipal government to order the Public Security Bureau to strictly punish them. (3) Regarding the case of restoring Fang Changda's freedom, it was stipulated that Yang and Huang would be responsible for sending Fang to this. For the above three articles, Yang and Huang signed their names to be responsible. For merchants who did not dare to operate, the Chamber of Commerce would be responsible for persuading them to resume business. The next day (23rd), all stores in the city resumed their old appearance. (May 23rd)

Closure of the Hujiatan Breach on the Yellow River in Shandong

Jinan Correspondence: The Hujiatan breach on the north bank of the lower reaches of the Yellow River in Lijin County was breached in the spring of the 17th year of the Republic. In the summer of the 18th year of the Republic, the provincial government spent 300,000 yuan but failed to close it. This spring, it was closed again, with an estimated cost of 119,000 yuan. However, soon after construction began, military affairs occurred in the area, making the project quite difficult. Fortunately, no matter which side the troops were on, they did not interfere with the closure project. The closure project started on the 24th and was completed. Because the banks of the Yellow River have become military areas, the report telegram arrived only yesterday (28th). The original text is as follows: (2) River Affairs Bureau Director Liu Junjian: At the time of Gengzi, the upper and lower corners of the beach point in the shallow water of the east dam were successively infested, leveling with the water. The upper corner of the beach point on the west dam was trapped by three feet. He immediately supervised the civil and military officials, soldiers, and laborers to add earth materials separately. At the time of Chen, the west dam began to stabilize. However, as the east dam was added, it was also trapped. By the time of noon, it was slightly calmer. Unexpectedly, the east wind supported the rapid current and the water rose by six inches. The depth of the breach increased from one zhang to one zhang eight or nine chi. He Nian and others, seeing the dangerous situation, were afraid that repeated scouring and protection would delay the opportunity. They immediately discussed with Committee Member Sun of the River Works Committee to occupy and close the breach at the time of Wei. Just as the material was being pressed and the earth was being swept, the wind became stronger and the water rose again. The difference between the water level before and after the sweep was four or five chi. The current in the breach was turbulent and dangerous. At the time of Xishi, the occupied sweep reached the bottom, and the back river sweep's eyes turned over and surged abnormally. Fortunately, the soldiers and laborers were brave, and the materials were available. On the one hand, they rushed to buy soil materials with cash and built a back dike. On the other hand, they transported and threw cattails and earth bags to block the sweep's eyes. By the time of Xu, the outflow gradually decreased, and the full period of drainage could be cut off in a few hours. Unexpectedly, a storm broke out, and the river water rose by more than two chi. Leaks appeared frequently in the occupied closure, and this blockage collapsed. All the workers, avoiding difficulties and dangers, were rushing to plug the gaps in the rain when a second new ditch was added. The fronts of the dikes of each project were all exposed to the water, and the wind and waves hit them at the same time. The protection was divided, but fortunately it was safe. Up to now, at the time of Chou, the leaks in the closure have gradually decreased, but the curtain water seepage has not stopped. It is estimated that the air can be closed at the time of noon. At this moment, we are still rushing to buy soil materials with cash to help the back dike to ensure safety and to avoid danger. Knocking from the breach closure project at Yin (2). Director Liu Junjian of the River Affairs Bureau, Ke Yin, please see the obstruction. Ke Yin's telegram should invite your perusal. The back dike at the closure continues to be rushed to be strengthened and soil is purchased with cash to actively surround the dike, and to use sacks of soil and yellow material to plug the leaks at any time. Up to the time of Wei, it is estimated that the rear dike has a width of about four zhang. All curtain water seepage has been completely cut off. After the closure of the air, in addition to increasing the height of each shallow water field, which has been completed for the past two months, we continue to rush to buy soil materials with cash to cultivate the dikes and protect them. I hereby report this telegram to you for your consideration. Knocking from the breach closure project.

Tragic Murder Case at Hongde Silver Shop in Hong Kong

Five Young Men in the Shop Were Killed

The Murderer Committed Suicide After the Murder, but Did Not Die

Hong Kong Correspondence: A tragic murder case suddenly occurred at the Hongde Silver Shop at 165 Queen's Road Central in Hong Kong at 4:30 AM yesterday. People in Hong Kong were shocked when they heard about it. It is understood that the murderer in this case was a former employee of the silver shop several years ago. He recently came to Hong Kong from his hometown and stayed at the silver shop. As for why he committed this brutal act, opinions vary. Now, the information gathered from various sources is described as follows:

The case occurred at the silver shop, which rents a four-story building. The second floor is the office of the chief manager, the third floor is the office of the deputy manager, and the fourth floor is where the partners live. There is also a kitchen on the fourth floor. After nightfall, the partners live on different floors. The chief and deputy managers are not in the shop, but they have several young sons who stay in the shop so they can go to school in the morning. The murderer arrived in Hong Kong a few days ago and stayed in the living room on the third floor last night. There are two rooms on that floor, and all the students were in the rooms. At 4:30 yesterday morning, screams for help were suddenly heard on the second and third floors of the shop. The partners in the shop were startled and immediately pressed the alarm bell in the shop. The central police station also received the news. At that time, everyone thought there was a fire and came out to see. Shortly after, the central police station dispatched a rapid response team by car and learned that a tragic murder case had occurred at the shop.

Police Investigation: At that time, the area around Hongde Silver Shop was surrounded by onlookers. Chinese, English, and Indian detectives rushed to the scene and cordoned off the surrounding area for investigation. At that time, traffic was temporarily cut off from Yongji Street in the east to Yonghe Street in the west. The police went up to each floor to investigate and found a corpse lying on a couch in the hall on the second floor, covered in blood. The hands were on the ground, and blood was still spurting from the throat. They then proceeded to the third floor and found four corpses lying in pools of blood, all in the two rooms on the third floor. Bloodstains were everywhere on the floor, and the sundries in the two rooms were stained red. Upon closer inspection, the fatal wounds on each of the four bodies were on the throat. In addition, one young man was seriously injured, and the murderer, Li Wen, also committed suicide and fell to the ground. An ambulance was called to the scene and the injured were sent to the National Hospital for treatment.

Details of the Murder: When the murderer committed the murder, everyone was asleep. It is estimated that there were a total of twenty people sleeping in the shop. Early that morning, the murderer secretly went up to the kitchen on the fourth floor and obtained four kitchen knives. He first went down to the third floor to commit the murder. At that time, in addition to the shop owner's sons, there were also several partners in the shop. The murderer brutally attacked the shop owner's sons. Because his methods were quick and decisive, he killed them with a single knife. Therefore, when he committed the murder on the third floor, although several lives were taken, no one knew about it. After the murderer brutally killed the young men on the third floor, he continued down to the second floor and killed Feng Xizhuo, the son of the chief manager. When Feng was attacked, his throat was cut and he could not make a sound. He struggled for a short time and then died. The murderer then slashed at Cheng Huiyu's young son, Cheng Zuhui. Cheng cried out in pain, and this tragedy was finally heard by everyone. The cook resisted the murderer: The partners heard the cries for help and got up to see what was happening. At that time, they saw the cook, Liu Yitian, standing in front of the murderer. The murderer, Li Wen, raised the knife and committed suicide, injuring his clothing. He then raised the knife and slashed at himself. The cook, Liu Yitian, stepped forward to resist and forcibly snatched the knife from him. The murderer then fell to the ground, blood gushing out. The partners rushed forward to examine him and saw that the murderer was still clutching the kitchen knife, which was covered in red. At that time, everyone thought the murderer was dead, but later they learned that he was still breathing.

Cause of the Case: After the incident, the reporter went to the shop to interview. According to the shop owner, Feng Yixi, the murderer was a former employee of the shop several years ago. He recently came to Hong Kong from his hometown and stayed at the shop. The day before this case occurred, the murderer said he had no job and was wandering around all day and decided to return home. Feng told him to stay a few more days. At that time, the murderer's intention to return home was very firm. He immediately took his luggage and left, but unexpectedly returned to the shop that night. The murderer had no quarrel with the five murdered men and the young master who was slashed, nor did he have any other incidents. Although the murderer was the concubine's uncle of Cheng Huiquan, the deputy manager of the shop, the tragic case was not related to Cheng personally. No one in the shop knew what caused the murderer to commit the crime. He had been in charge of the shop for several years without any incidents. The purpose of his murder was probably not to rob the shop of money. At that time, no one saw him take any other actions, only that he committed suicide.

Names of the Dead and Injured: It is understood that a total of five people died in this case, one was injured, and the murderer was injured. The names are as follows: (1) Feng Xizhuo, 19 years old, from Jiujiang Shiwan, Nanhai, and son of the manager Feng Litang. He studied at Wah Yan College and was killed on the second floor. (2) Cheng Zubei, 15 years old, from Jiujiang, suffered serious head injuries and died on the spot. (3) Cheng Pan, 14 years old, from Jiujiang, suffered head and chest injuries and died in the ambulance on the way. The two individuals in items one, two and three are the sons of the deputy manager Cheng Huiquan. (4) Cheng Yongjie, 14 years old, from Jiujiang, suffered head injuries and died on the spot. (5) Cheng Yongyuan, 13 years old, suffered head injuries and died on the spot. The individuals in items four and five are the sons of the buyer, Cheng Dizhi. (6) Cheng Zuhui, 16 years old, suffered body injuries and is currently hospitalized. (7) Murderer Li Wen, 27 years old, cut his own throat and was injured. (25th)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang

Compilation of Bandit Cases in Fengjing: On the evening of the 29th, at about 1:00 AM, the home of Shen Songqing, a farmer in Qingliang Lane, Yaocheng, Beidaibang, Fengjing, was robbed by more than ten bandits armed with weapons. Shen Songqing's son, Jin Yuan, was tied up and shot. After Jin Yuan was kidnapped, he was sent to a boat and escaped by swimming at dawn. He was discovered by the bandits who chased him and fired shots. Unfortunately, one shot pierced his chest and another his foot. Seeing that the hostage was seriously injured, the bandits abandoned him and left. It is now known that the injured have been sent to the hospital for treatment. However, the injuries of Shen Songqing and his son are very serious and their lives are in danger. Furthermore, the Fengjing Joint Defense Office previously destroyed a bandit den at the junction of Songjiang and Qingpu counties, rescued hostage Wu Guoqing, captured bandits Feng Youcai and Shen Zhuqing, and seized three rifles and one bandit boat. It is now heard that the office interrogated bandits Feng Youcai and others, who confessed that Li Fuqing was the bandit leader, there were more than 20 people in the gang, they had 12 guns, and they were hired to guard Wu, and that they knew nothing about the rest. After interrogation, they prepared a document and sent it to the Shanghai Garrison Command for legal action. A fugitive police officer was captured and escorted back to the county. Yuan Zhenxian, a policeman from the second squadron of the county police team, was from Fuyang, Zhejiang. He had been with the team for only a short time. On the 19th, while on patrol, he claimed to need to urinate, took his gun and escaped. The team searched for him but could not find him. His guarantor, Ma Liansheng, was ordered to surrender him and a wanted notice was issued. It is now learned that a fellow villager of Yuan's from the team secretly went to Fuyang to investigate and found Yuan back in Fuyang, eating noodles in a noodle shop. He was immediately arrested and sent to Squadron Leader Song Yin of Songjiang on the 30th. According to Yuan Zhenxian's confession, the Mauser gun had been sold for 105 yuan. The squadron leader punished Yuan for violating military discipline and beat him with military sticks, and then sent him to the county government for punishment.

Bandits Set Fire to Wuxutou: Since the bandit Tai Bao Ashu occupied Qianjiawei and the surrounding area in Nanxiang, all those with some wealth have sought to move away. It is heard that bandits set fire to Wuxutou the night before last. Wuxutou is about two li from Langxia. Although it is not a market town, the houses are well-organized, which is rare in the countryside. Many wealthy people have moved away, but He Lansheng's family is in modest circumstances. He had previously received a letter from the bandits demanding 10,000 yuan. After receiving the letter, He left home to avoid them, but he had no way to respond, which angered the bandits. The night before last, they prepared several cans of kerosene and set fire to his entire family, turning it into ruins, and also affecting the Zou family, causing them considerable losses.

Jinshan

Bandits Gathered to Rob Jinshan Nanxiang: Tai Bao Ashu, who gathered bandits from Jiajiawei Bridge in Nanxiang, Jinshan, has repeatedly robbed important towns in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. Since Zhejiang troops have repeatedly searched and suppressed the area, they once fled into Taihu Lake. When the Taihu Bandit Suppression Command was established and guarded the important passes, they could not succeed and planned to change their route back to their lair. They passed through Chenmu and were spotted by Su troops who launched a head-on attack. All of the more than 20 bandit ships were sunk. It is heard that the stolen goods on the ships were worth a great deal of money. They then fled back to their old lair, and many of their gang members returned. Fearing that Zhejiang troops would come to search and suppress them again, on the 16th of this month, Tai Bao Ashu went to the Langxia district to drive out the abbot of the Jizi Nunnery and used it as their headquarters. Every night, they gave speeches in the nunnery. It seems that they have an organized secretariat, which is reportedly managed by Yan Shusheng. There are a total of about 300 bandits. A branch office was set up at the north end of Shantang, which is managed by the second leader, Zhuluo Aimei. Many wealthy families in the area have received letters of extortion. Now, those who are said to have assets in the surrounding area have moved away. The bandits call themselves the Songhu Guerrilla Team.

Fengxian

Imprisonment of Father's Concubine Causes Lawsuit: A few days ago, it was rumored in the teahouses and wineries of Nanqiao that Zhuang Jieqing, a resident of Nanjie, had abused his father's concubine and privately imprisoned her. At the same time, his neighbor, surnamed Wang, told the former director of the Songzhang Water and Land Salt Smuggling Bureau, Li Tianmin, the facts he had witnessed and asked him to help rescue her. Li, feeling that justice could not be denied, reported it to the First District Office. District Chief Jiang Rongchu sent a letter to the County Public Security Bureau Director Li, who dispatched inspectors Tan and Chen to intervene. However, Zhuang's house was deep and far away, making it impossible to investigate. They replied stating the matter was well-founded and should be handled. Now it is learned that Zhuang has accused Li in court of fabricating facts and falsely accusing him, intending to defraud him. Li, although the matter does not concern him, is unwilling to show weakness to protect humanity. A craftsman who made the wooden prisoner testified as a witness and filed a counter-suit the day before yesterday. Magistrate Shen has scheduled a court hearing for June 5th. It is thought that the truth of the case will not be difficult to reveal at that time.

Yinglong Temple Reported Another Theft: There have been more than 20 theft cases of various sizes in the county, and most of the incidents have occurred in the area where Songjiang, Jinshan, Nanqiao, and Fengxian counties border each other. Last night, at 9:00 PM, bandits carried out a robbery in Yinglongmiao Town, which is located on the Song-Feng border. The town has no defense and is a rural market town that counties cannot resist. When Petty Officer Bu of the Ruanxiang police team reported the incident, the police squad leader, Yang Xingsheng, went to encircle and suppress them, but they had already fled far away. It was found that five families in Fengjing and two families in Songjing had been robbed, each losing about two or three hundred yuan. The County Government sent a judicial clerk to the village yesterday to investigate the robbery cases in the 39th district, including the families of Chen and Xia. In the case of Xi Yusun's family in Zhangjiatang, the already captured thieves were brought together to have the victims identify them yesterday evening, and they were sentenced to imprisonment.

Suzhou

The Ministry of Justice has commissioned an investigation into the Jiangsu Third Branch Prison on Sijian Lane and the High Court Detention Center, where incidents of prison riots have occurred, and someone has allegedly been distributing leaflets outside detailing the alleged oppression of prisoners by the guards. The Ministry of Judicial Administration also received these leaflets. Therefore, on the 30th, they specifically appointed Section Chief Liao to come to Suzhou to join Secretary Ni of the High Court in investigating the situation at the prison.

The Ministry of Military Affairs has telegraphed orders to prepare a rear hospital. The county government received a telegram yesterday from the Commander-in-Chief and the Ministry of Military Affairs stating that due to the wounded soldiers at the front lines, they plan to transport them to Suzhou for treatment. They were instructed to find buildings capable of accommodating more than 1,000 people and to prepare a rear hospital with medical personnel, and to order the police to be responsible for escorting and guarding the wounded soldiers upon their arrival. After receiving the telegram, County Magistrate Huang immediately summoned Presidents Wu and Zhang of the county hospital to discuss and scheduled a meeting of various agencies in three days to prepare.

A Central Investigator Commits Suicide in Suzhou. Zhong Shicai, a 24-year-old investigator from the Central Headquarters of the Capital Kuomintang, arrived in Suzhou on the afternoon of the 29th with two pieces of luggage. He stayed in room 30 of the Wujun Hotel outside Changmen, wearing a Western suit. He showed no signs of distress that evening, but his pockets were empty. The next day, Zhong took a Western-style overcoat to a pawn shop to raise funds for expenses. However, because Suzhou pawn shops generally do not accept Western suits, Zhong returned to the hotel feeling depressed. The hotel accountant, Pu Yiyun, then lent him one dollar. Zhong used the money to buy a bottle of Huadiao wine outside in the evening, returned to the hotel, drank only one-third of it, and went to sleep. Yesterday morning (the 31st) at around 9 a.m., the tea server Xu Changsheng opened the door when Zhong still hadn't gotten up and saw Zhong soundly asleep, heard him breathing continuously, and noticed white foam coming from his mouth. Knowing something was wrong, he reported to the head accountant, Pu Yiyun. Pu immediately hired a car to send Zhong to the Xiao Yong Hospital for treatment. Two empty bottles of tranquilizer pills were found in the room. After Zhong was sent to the hospital, Dr. Gu Suyong injected him with a rescue antidote, but he was still not out of danger. A suicide note was found beside him, stating: "I am a disciple of the Premier and a student of Whampoa. I am not disheartened by setbacks, and I also know that those who take revolution as their profession must maintain an optimistic attitude at all times and in all places. I wanted to resume military life and strive to kill the enemy as the vanguard for the people, but I was unable to fulfill my wish due to illness. My body is full of sins, and redemption is impossible. Everyone has their own aspirations, and no one should be forced," and so on. Pu Yiyun of the hotel, knowing that Zhong was an investigator from the Central Kuomintang Headquarters, immediately telegraphed the Central Kuomintang Headquarters to send someone to Suzhou to handle the matter.

Changzhou

Multiple Robberies Occur Outside the East Gate. The homes of Fan Yuhai, Fan Lin, Da Fan, Fan Shunfa, and others in Fanjiatang outside the East Gate of Wuyi were robbed of valuables and miscellaneous items the night before last. Yesterday (the 30th), the victims claimed that many of the robbers were familiar faces, but they were afraid of retaliation and dared not report the case. Furthermore, Zhu Lansheng's family in Gaotoufen Village nearby recently sold cocoons for 200 yuan, which was coveted by bandits. On the 28th, 126 yuan and 10 jiao of the remaining cocoon money in the family were robbed. The victim also did not report the case.

The County Government Sends Police to Investigate a Kidnapping Case. It has been learned that a kidnapping gang was broken up at Shizhutou outside the North Gate of Wuyi. Magistrate Wu, considering the complexity of the case, interrogated victim Liu Jinsheng and others on the 30th, and further questioned the bandits Chao Xingkun and others. He also specifically sent political police and others to the countryside to investigate. The investigation revealed that on the day of the kidnapping, thirteen bandits wearing yellow and black military uniforms went to Tanjia Village and kidnapped the family of Liu Jinsheng. The doors of the three buildings were sealed with wooden boards and nails. The police also brought back a proclamation from the bandit suppression department to the county for review.

Wuxi

Wuxi Prepares to Establish a Continental Bank. Ye Juexiao, the president of the Continental Bank of Shanghai, decided to establish a Wuxi branch in Wuxi to expand business, as the county is densely populated, industry and commerce are thriving, and water and land transportation are convenient. Fang Licun has been appointed as the branch manager. The branch will be located at the original site of Hengyuan Cang Paper Shop on North Tang East Street. Workers are currently being hired to renovate the building, and the official opening is scheduled after the end of the lunar year.

Strange and Suspicious Robbery. Yesterday afternoon at around 1:00 PM, Cao Haochu, a partner at the Lu Hengxing Sand Casting Factory, suddenly went to the Sixth Branch of the Public Security Bureau on Guangqin Road to report that he (Cao claimed) had recently collected 285 yuan in banknotes and over 200 yuan in silver dollars in the Qingyang Township area bordering Cheng and Wuxi. He was walking back to the factory after arriving in Wuxi by boat when he was suddenly stopped by three bandits near Liangba. They silenced him, searched his body, and robbed all the money he had collected. The bandits also fired a handgun, but luckily, it did not hit him, although there were four holes in the sleeve of his left arm. He requested that the police be dispatched to pursue the bandits. After receiving the report, Director Duan of the branch immediately led the police and Cao Haochu to the scene to investigate. Qian Tianxiong, the Inspector General of the Public Security Bureau, Ni Gusheng, the Detective Chief of the Second Water Police District, and Liao Dajin of the Police Brigade Headquarters also rushed to investigate after hearing the news. Residents in the Liangba area claimed that there had been no robberies and that they had not heard any gunshots. After carefully examining the four holes in Cao's sleeve, it was determined that they were not bullet holes, and the circumstances were highly suspicious. Duan, the branch director, took Cao Haochu back to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Two Families Robbed in Tuli Lane. More than ten bandits broke into the home of Tu Meifang, a resident of Tuli Lane in the Third District (Yangming Township), who was engaged in farming, at midnight on the 27th. Meifang and others were already asleep when they heard the noise and were frightened. The bandits threatened them with guns and then searched everywhere for an hour before going to the home of Tu Fuquan next door to rob for about half an hour. They then left with their loot, shouting and screaming. After an investigation, it was found that more than 500 yuan in cocoon money and over 100 yuan in clothing and jewelry had been stolen from the two families, for a total loss of over 600 yuan. The case has been reported to the county for strict investigation.

The Construction Committee Organizes a Five-County Irrigation Area. The Qishuyan Power Plant of the Central Construction Committee covers the counties of Wu and Xi with power lines running through them. More than 560 li of urban and rural areas in the two counties have been electrified, with more than 20 townships using electric power for agricultural irrigation, mostly in the southwest townships of Wujin. Wuxi has been piloting the program for two years, but it has not yet become widespread, with fewer than 10,000 mu using electric pumps for irrigation. Wu Yulin, the director of the power plant, has been striving to promote the program and previously presented a proposal to Zhang Jingjiang, chairman of the Construction Committee, to pilot the first irrigation area in Wuxi, Wujin, and Yixing counties to promote electric pumping and improve farmland irrigation. Chairman Zhang presented the proposal to the Construction Committee, which resolved to approve it and decided to promote electric pumping and operate long-distance trams to facilitate land transportation. After several discussions, it was decided to designate Wuxi, Wujin, Jiangyin, Changshu, and Yixing as an irrigation area and to open long-distance trams on the Yichang Provincial Road and Xicheng Highway to facilitate transportation in the four counties, with the aim of developing agriculture, water conservancy, land transportation, and electricity to the greatest extent possible. The financial issues have been discussed with Chu Minyi, a member of the Construction Committee, and various countries, and it has been decided to allocate a portion of the refunded Boxer Indemnity for operating expenses.

Shocking News of a Collection Agent Shot to Death. A collection agent from a certain store, Mr. Jia (about 30 years old), was returning from the countryside to the city yesterday (the 31st) at around 1:00 PM when he was suddenly shot in the throat by thugs in the Lengdu Bridge area outside the South Gate. He fell to the ground in extreme pain. Xi Laohu, the local Tuba, hired someone to carry the injured man to the Puren Hospital for treatment. However, due to the severity of his injuries, he died near Yangyaowan. The Tuba reported the incident to Director Zhu of the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau, who dispatched Patrol Captain Cai and Officer Li to investigate. Seventy yuan in banknotes and 18 jiao in bills were found in the victim's left sock. The victim had pockmarks on his face, gold teeth in his mouth, and was wearing a woolen single shirt. Patrol Captain Cai reported back to the bureau after the investigation, and the Tuba also reported the incident to the county government, requesting that someone be sent to conduct an autopsy to assist in the arrest of the murderer.

Nantong

Organizing a Coastal Patrol Team for Five Counties. Coastal banditry has resurged in the five counties of Jiangbei: Nantong, Rugao, Dongtai, Haimen, and Qidong. The Civil Affairs Department has ordered the county magistrates of the five counties to discuss and organize a coastal patrol team for the five counties to be established within half a month. County Magistrate Zhang has gathered 20,000 yuan in initial expenses based on the resolutions of the five county magistrates, and the provincial government will allocate firearms.

Bank Warehouse Grain Mortgage Case. It was reported that a grain merchant had mortgaged 1,197 shi of rice in the Jiangsu Bank warehouse, which was accused of hoarding for speculation. The county council decided to order the rice to be sold at a reduced price of two yuan per shi. The grain merchant refused and telegraphed the Jiangsu Bank headquarters to the Civil Affairs Department, which ordered the county government to investigate the matter fairly, as grain mortgages were considered a legitimate business, and at a time when rice prices were soaring, rice warehouses were needed to provide relief.

Military and Police Jointly Suppress Sea Bandits in Lüsi. Sea bandits are rampant in the Lüsi area, having recently killed more than 20 male and female hostages and burned many fishing boats. The Navy Department has dispatched the Yongsheng shallow-water patrol ship to cooperate with the Fourth District Department of the Wusong Water Police to dispatch the 17th and 18th patrol boat teams, along with the National Army and Provincial Police stationed in Tong, to encircle and suppress the bandits. The county police and militia are responsible for blocking the fleeing bandits.

Jiangyin

Taking Advantage of the Yarn Factory Strike. Male and female workers at a yarn factory are demanding that the factory increase the rice subsidy by two jiao per person per day due to the high price of rice. The factory refused the request as being too harsh, and the workers went on strike yesterday (the 30th). Zhong Jianhui and others from the County Kuomintang Restructuring Committee went to the factory outside the North Gate in the morning to mediate and negotiated with worker representatives Ren Ruisheng, Shi Zhao, Da Yuan, Amei, and others without result. However, while they were discussing, most of the workers suddenly entered the city and first went to the county high school to request the use of the auditorium for a meeting, but were rejected by the high school. The workers then went outside and discovered reactionary leaflets scattered everywhere. The workers then went to the stadium to hold a meeting. County Magistrate Li, upon hearing this, immediately led armed police to the stadium to disperse the meeting, citing the martial law imposed during the May Thirtieth Movement. All male and female workers were searched, and Fan Rongyi was detained for tearing up a letter. The phrases were mostly incomprehensible after piecing together the torn letter. Shen Zhangbao and eight other suspects were also detained. County Magistrate Li requested that a platoon of soldiers from the stationed 8th Company of the Military Police assist in searching the house outside the North Gate, but nothing was found. The worker representatives Ren Ruisheng, Li San, Zhao Akun, Sun Huichen, Tang Xijing, Shi Zhao, Liu Ada, and others were detained in the Public Security Bureau for temporary detention and strict interrogation to determine whether they were suspected of being reactionary and the origin of the reactionary printed materials. The County Kuomintang convened a meeting of labor and management to mediate the labor dispute, and the factory agreed to provide subsidized rice within ten days to meet the workers' needs. The armed forces were on special alert last night to prevent any unforeseen events.

Danyang

Bandit Forces Resurge in Maoshan. On the 24th, a large band of bandits numbering over 100, all wearing straw hats and plain clothes of various colors, and mostly armed with Mauser pistols, along with more than 20 rifles, arrived in the Maoshan area bordering Ju and Danyang and went to the Liufang Palace to plunder at will, shooting and wounding a Daoist priest. They then regrouped, blew their horns, and went down the mountain to rob Xitashan Village in Jintan County, killing the victim, Wang. The bandits are still entrenched in the Xitashan area and are extremely rampant. Yanling Town in our county, which is close to Maoshan, is afraid of disturbances, and the town's public security branch and the business community have taken strict precautions.

Wenchang Pavilion Burned Down. Wenchang Pavilion, located a few dozen steps in front of the Confucius Temple in the west of the city, was a one-story building of exquisite architecture overlooking the pond and was a scenic highlight of the county. Yesterday at 5:00 PM, several children climbed up to enjoy the view and dropped a cigarette butt, causing a fire. Although the fire brigades of various shops made every effort to extinguish the fire, the fire was too fierce, and the entire pavilion was reduced to ashes.

Reactionary Leaflets Discovered in the City. Reactionary leaflets were scattered on the ground in Beicaoxiang and other places in the county yesterday. A student from the Lutaixiang Shoe Store who happened to be passing by bent down to pick them up and was spotted by a guard, who took the student and the leaflets to the county for interrogation.

Yangzhou

Fishing Boats Robbed in Succession. At around 12:00 PM on the 29th, a boat carrying eggs from Gaoyou to Dongguan was robbed by bandits near the South Salt Office north of Wutaishan, who looted all the rice and silver dollars. The boatman, Tang San, unloaded the eggs and left Yangzhou. It was also learned that a fishing boat was robbed in the same area the day before.

Zhenjiang

Agricultural Hall Prepares for Product Exhibition. The Agricultural Products Exhibition Hall of the Department of Agriculture and Mining is about to open. Although the items collected last year and sent to the West Lake Exposition have been donated to the hall by the producers, they have been left for a long time and are inevitably old and decayed. It is still necessary to sort and replenish them to make them perfect. Therefore, the provincial and county departments were specifically ordered yesterday to select and prepare the latest products, make specimens and designs, and decorate them, and to send them to the province within 20 days after receiving the order for forwarding and display for observation.

Bandits Discovered Again in Gaozi Township. A band of more than 200 bandits suddenly appeared in Wulicun, Gaozi Township, Zhenjiang, at around 8:00 PM yesterday, carrying torches and robbing wildly. The local security team went to encircle and suppress them, but the bandits dared to fire their guns and resist arrest. The two sides exchanged fire for about 20 minutes before the bandits were defeated. The team has telegraphed the provincial authorities, requesting that troops be sent immediately to assist in the suppression to maintain order.

Jiaxing

District Offices to Be Established by a Deadline. The Jiaxing Autonomous Region has been determined, and the entire region will be divided into seven districts. The locations of the district offices have also been determined. It has been learned that the county government has ordered the district chiefs to establish all district offices by June 1. The county government originally planned to allocate the remaining funds from the land survey reports to cover the operating expenses, but the provincial government has ordered the county to report that the review and re-measurement procedures have not yet been carried out, and it cannot be considered that there are any remaining funds at this time. Therefore, the county government telegraphed the County Funds and Property Management Committee yesterday to allocate the previously approved 2,313 yuan and 56 jiao and 6 fen of the county's local public funds to ensure the establishment is completed on schedule.

Investigation of Education Bureau Director Being Sued. Jiaxing Education Bureau Director Ren Xuan was recently accused of fraudulently enticing farmer Ma Deyou from Fenghuangqiao to the bureau under the pretext of a meeting while clearing the school fields, and then illegally detaining Deyou. Ma Deyou then hired Xuan Qugao to file a complaint with the court, accusing Director Ren of illegal detention and obstruction of freedom, and requesting the court to punish him according to the law. It is learned that after receiving the complaint, the local branch of the High Court's Prosecutor's Office sent a letter to the county government to investigate the case and has now received a reply. Therefore, the branch has issued a summons and scheduled the investigation to begin on June 9.

Huzhou

Bandits Extort Huge Sums from Zhongjun Town. Zhongjun Town near Linghu, Huzhou, has 50 to 60 pawnshops and shops. The town has been free of bandits since the Taiping Rebellion. Although there have been many bandits in various places in recent years, the town has remained peaceful, and the merchants and residents have lived in peace. Unexpectedly, a certain gentleman in the town recently received a letter from the bandits, borrowing 30,000 yuan to meet their urgent needs, to be delivered at Boshu Temple on the 28th. The person delivering the money must wear a long shirt, carry a rattan basket in his left hand, and hold a cigar in his right hand as a sign. If the money is not delivered by the deadline, a large group will be sent to the town to collect it. The gentleman was extremely alarmed after reading the letter and immediately convened a meeting of merchants and residents. After much deliberation, they submitted a request to the provincial government to send troops to guard the town to prevent unforeseen events.

Xiaoshan

The Seawall is in Danger During the Plum Rains. The plum rains have been continuous, and the Jiang tide has been surging, making the Qiantang Seawall extremely dangerous. It has been reported that many sections of the seawall in Xixing and Wenyan are broken and the situation is dangerous. The villagers along the seawall, considering that the matter concerns the lives and residences of the people, have reported the dangerous sections of the seawall to the Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau for consideration of repairs to avoid danger.

Ningbo

Hong Yuchang Silk Store Also Ran Aground Yesterday. Hong Yuchang Silk Store on Dongmen Street in Ningbo City is owned by Hong Cangting. This time, because of the successive collapses of Geng Yu, Tong Kang, and Hong Tai, Hong Yuchang was indirectly affected as a shareholder. The various money shops that Hong Yuchang Silk Store dealt with cautiously stopped paying their debts. Yesterday, they also declared that they were running aground and stopped doing business. There are no major discrepancies in the amounts.

Two Robbery Cases in Yinxi and Yaobei. Hong, who runs a cool hat shop behind the Bailongwang Temple in Yinxi, is quite well-off. At midnight on May 26, six bandits speaking with a Taiwanese accent suddenly broke open the gate with wooden sticks. Hong was just settling accounts in Yong that day, leaving only women and children at home, who were robbed as the bandits overturned boxes and chests, stealing more than 60 silver dollars and a pair of gold bracelets before leaving with torches. Shui Gen from Yuyao runs a wine, rice, and sundries shop in Xiaocaoe Temple in the north of Yuyao. The shop has been open for many years and is quite prosperous, which has attracted the covetousness of bandits. At about 10:00 PM the other day, the shop had closed its doors and was preparing to go to bed when five bandits speaking with foreign accents suddenly came, asking to buy melon seeds as a pretext to open the door and loot wildly, resulting in the loss of silver, clothes, and other items.

Local News

Today's Commemoration of Premier's Interment

The City Kuomintang Committee is holding a memorial service

At 9 a.m. in the auditorium of the committee

Today marks the first anniversary of the interment of the Premier of the Chinese Kuomintang. The Municipal Executive Committee has set today at 9:00 a.m. to hold a memorial service in the City Kuomintang Committee on the third floor of Lin Yinzhi Road, Ximen. All schools, organizations, and Kuomintang branches at all levels must send representatives to participate to show their commemoration. It is also heard that the Municipal Propaganda Department has prepared a variety of propaganda materials to be distributed to the guests at the meeting. The order of service, slogans, and mottoes are as follows:

Order of Service: (1) All stand at attention (2) Sing the Kuomintang anthem (3) Pay the highest respect to the Kuomintang flag, the national flag, and the Premier's portrait (4) The chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will (5) Silence (6) The chairman reports (7) Speeches (8) Shout slogans (9) Dismissal

Slogans and Mottoes: (A) Slogans: 1. The Premier's spirit is immortal 2. Continue the Premier's fearless spirit 3. Strive for political tutelage and construction 4. May 30th Incident Commemoration

Memorial service held the day before yesterday

Public memorial service for the martyred heroes

Report on the memorial service

The day before yesterday was the fifth anniversary of the May 30th Incident. A memorial service was held at the Penglai Grand Theater on Penglai Road in the South City at 9:00 a.m. on the day before yesterday. About 2,000 representatives from all walks of life attended. Chen Dezheng presided over the meeting, and Yang Qingyuan delivered a speech on behalf of the Municipal Kuomintang Committee. Ye Huijun and others also delivered speeches. The Municipal Executive Committee's Propaganda Department specially printed a variety of propaganda materials for the May 30th commemoration and distributed them on the spot. Each representative received one copy of the Municipal Propaganda Department's "Era" bi-monthly magazine and a pamphlet. Finally, Lu Jingshi, Ma Zhiying, Yang Qingyuan, Chen Kecheng, and ten others were designated to hold a public memorial service at the Martyrs' Cemetery in Zhabei. Details are listed below:

Order of Service: (1) All stand at attention (2) Play mournful music (3) Sing the Kuomintang anthem (4) Pay the highest respect to the Kuomintang flag, the national flag, and the Premier's portrait (5) The chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will (6) Observe three minutes of silence for the dead martyrs (7) The chairman reports (8) The representative of the Municipal Kuomintang Committee delivers a speech (9) Speeches (10) Shout slogans (11) Dismissal

Public Memorial Service for the Martyred Heroes

At 10:30 a.m. the day before yesterday, another public memorial service was held at the May 30th Martyrs' Cemetery at Fangjia Muqiao in Zhabei. Representatives from various agencies, organizations, and Kuomintang branches at all levels participated, and the May 30th Incident Victims' Families Association and the families of the martyred heroes also came to the cemetery to pay their respects. The order was solemn. The public memorial service is recorded below:

Cemetery Arrangement: The May 30th Martyrs' Cemetery was built on May 25, 1928. A memorial tower was built in front of the tomb, towering into the clouds. The cemetery is surrounded by walls. In January of this year, the May 30th Incident Victims' Families Association negotiated with the British Public Works Department and resolved the compensation issue. After the families decided, in addition to repaying the 10,000 yuan previously advanced for the construction of the cemetery, they also allocated 10,000 yuan to add to the repairs of the cemetery, so the cemetery building became more tidy. At 7:00 a.m. the day before yesterday, the representatives of the Families Association, Hu Changsheng and Chen Fucai, Secretary Zhou Zaisheng, and staff members Wang Dianyin and Sun Guangfu, arrived first to make careful arrangements. A horizontal banner was hung at the gate, reading "Public Memorial Ceremony for the May 30th Martyrs by the People of All Circles in Shanghai." The stone steps in front of the tomb were hastily built yesterday and completed. A couplet was hung on both sides of the tomb, reading "The blue blood is buried forever, leaving only a sad history of Shanghai, the monument stands tall, awakening the national spirit of China." A canopy was erected over the tomb, and the Premier's portrait was hung on the tombstone, with the Kuomintang flag and the national flag on both sides. A sacrificial table was set up in front of the tombstone, with two wreaths in front, one offered by the Municipal Government and one offered by the May 30th Families Association. A guest seat and a family seat were placed on the left side.

Families Paying Respects: Wang Zhou, mother of martyr Wang Kuibao, Wang Guisheng, brother of martyr Wang Kuibao, Shi Zhangfu, adopted son of martyr Shi Songsheng, Yao Tao, mother of martyr Yao Shunqing, Wang Dan, wife of martyr Wang Jifu, Wu Shunbao, father of martyr Wu Zhenghua, Zhan Chunting, father of martyr Zhan Chongbing, Yang Lianchun, brother of martyr Yang Lianfa, Chen Zhaorong, brother of martyr Chen Zhaochang, Hua Zonghai, brother of martyr Hua Zongyun, Tan Yuanji, father of martyr Tan Quanfu, Wei Guoxiang, brother of martyr Wei Guoping, and more than 20 people, including Hu Chang, Chen Fucai, Secretary Zhou Zaisheng, and staff members Sun Guangfu and Wang Dianyin, representatives of the Families Association.

Postponement of the Disbandment of the Likin Tax Conference

Third Preparatory Meeting Held Today

The Conference Date Will Be No Later Than Ten Days

The National Likin Tax Disbandment Conference was originally scheduled to hold its opening ceremony at 10:00 AM today in the auditorium of the Central Bank in Shanghai. However, as of yesterday, the representatives from the provincial finance bureaus and the special commissioners of the Ministry of Finance were unable to arrive in time, resulting in a very small number of attendees. It was estimated that less than half of the representatives would be present today. Therefore, the conference date has been postponed, and a third preparatory meeting will be held today. A public telegram will be sent in the name of the conference to the provincial finance bureaus and special commissioners of the Ministry of Finance, requesting that they immediately appoint the section chiefs or division chiefs in charge of the Likin tax in their respective provinces to come to Shanghai as soon as possible for consultation and reporting on the income situation of the Likin tax in each province. This will facilitate the collection of opinions from all representatives, the formulation of proposals, and their submission to the National Government for implementation. According to Mr. Li Jiming, a counselor dispatched by the Ministry of Finance to Shanghai to preside over the conference, the conference date has been postponed for several days, and the meeting will be held after more than half of the representatives from various provinces have arrived. Therefore, it will be no later than ten days. Representatives from remote provinces who are unable to send representatives due to travel difficulties will submit written reports. (New Shanghai News Agency)

History of the Party Department The preparation of the Naval Party Department began on April 10th of the 16th year, when the director of the Naval Political Department, Ye Yangmin, was temporarily appointed as the preparatory director of the special party department, and Zheng Youyi, Jiang Bi, Zhuang Ye, Baoqi, and fourteen others were appointed as members of the preparatory committee. The office was established in Gaochang Temple in this city on the same day. On October 26th, the seal was issued by the central government and put into use on the same day. In November, the regulations of the preparatory committee were revised, adding four members. On December 26th, at the special meeting, Yang Shuzhuang was elected as the chairman of the standing committee, and Ye Yangmin, Zheng Youyi, Sun Chengsi, and Ye Baoqi were elected as standing committee members. Zheng Youyi also served as secretary-general. On the following day, they took office at the Jiangnan Shipyard. Therefore, actively solicited party members to expand the organization. In the 17th year, the general registration of the entire army was held, and after it was stopped in December, party departments at all levels were established one after another. On March 5th of the 18th year, the first representative conference of party members of the entire army was convened, and the first executive and supervisory committees were produced. Tomorrow is the second representative conference of party members of the entire army, and the second executive and supervisory committees will be re-elected.

Letter to the World's People from the Indian Alliance

The National Communications Agency yesterday released a letter to the world's people from the Indian Alliance. This letter is a booklet printed in both Chinese and English on two pages bound together. It first describes the poverty of India after being ruled by England, then describes how Indians repeatedly negotiated with the British authorities in the hope that the British would realize their error, but the British oppression intensified. Finally, it states that Indians no longer hope for the British to realize their error and will continue to fight for freedom, hoping to receive assistance.

Yangtze River Fares Drop Significantly Starting Today

Months of Disputes Resolved

Chinese and Foreign Steamship Companies Form Alliance

Yangtze River boat tickets from six Chinese and foreign companies have always been uniformly managed and could not be privately lowered or raised. Since the dissolution of the Public Ticket Bureau, British and Japanese steamship companies have regained control of ticket sales to compete for passengers with Chinese-owned ships. This has led to inconsistencies in ticket prices, with each company setting its own rates. With the recent rise in the price of gold, steamship ticket prices have generally increased, with North and South China Sea routes already increasing by 10-20%. Initially, British merchants advocated raising Yangtze River ticket prices to maintain profits, with Jardine Matheson taking the lead. However, the Taikoo Dockyard argued that passenger traffic on the Yangtze River this year was not as good as in previous years and insisted on maintaining the original prices. The Japanese company Nisshin Steamship Company fundamentally opposed the British proposal, stating that the current situation was such that both cargo and passenger traffic on the Yangtze River had declined, and ticket prices should be lowered to attract passengers. Therefore, opinions diverged and no agreement could be reached. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company did not express its position. For months, the disputes remained unresolved. Finally, in late May, the four companies, Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, Nisshin, and China Merchants, held several meetings to publicly discuss the long-delayed issue of rising and falling ticket prices. The majority decided that the main reason for the significant decrease in passengers in the Gan and Wan ports this year was local unrest, and the situation in Hankou was further complicated by the ongoing Ping-Han Railway war, making it difficult to raise prices immediately. Therefore, Jardine Matheson's proposal to raise prices could not be sustained. Starting today, Yangtze River ticket prices from Shanghai to Hankou will be reduced, with a 20% discount on the original price. However, round-trip tickets previously sold at a 30% discount will now be cancelled and must be purchased at full price. The agreement was signed by the four companies. The months-long dispute over Yangtze River ticket prices has now come to an end, and the competitive situation of mutually raising and lowering prices since the dissolution of the Public Ticket Bureau has also ended. Starting June 1st, Yangtze River ship tickets will return to the alliance status of three years ago. This is also a major issue in the Yangtze River shipping industry. The new ticket prices are listed below (the following are the first-class ticket prices for the main dining room):

New Yangtze River Freight News

Downstream Freight Rates Reduced The original freight rate for cotton yarn shipped from Shanghai to Yichang on the upper reaches of the Yangtze River was 3 taels, 9 mace, and 6 fen per piece. Later, when the river water receded and Chinese ships stopped operating, the price increased by 30% to 5 taels, 1 mace, and 5 fen per piece. Now, due to the high water level in the upper reaches and the resumption of operations by many Chinese ships, the number of departures from Shanghai to Yichang has increased daily. The six companies in this city have reduced prices due to the abundance of ships and the scarcity of goods. The result of yesterday's discussion was that the freight rate for cotton yarn from Shanghai to Yichang will be calculated at 2 taels and 5 mace plus 30%, and the actual price from today will be 3 taels, 2 mace, and 5 fen, a reduction of 1 tael and 9 mace per piece according to the fixed amount.

Increased Freight Rates for Sugar Recently, it has been the peak season for shipping white sugar to the Yangtze River. Yesterday, the six companies discussed increasing freight rates and changing to new regulations. The previous method of charging based on weight for each piece of 100 jin has been changed to charging per piece, divided into large pieces (140 jin to 165 jin) and small pieces (within 140 jin). The new regulations and price increases will take effect today, with an increase of approximately 20% over the original rate. The details are recorded as follows (Destination) (Large Piece Price) (Small Piece Price) (Original Price per 100 Jin) Fen Fen Fen

Municipal Land Bureau Consolidates Tax Revenue

Land Collected Through Auction, Exchange, or Donation

Transfer Tax Collected, No Need to Re-Establish Contract

The Municipal Land Bureau handles the purchase, auction, exchange, donation, and acquisition of land by various agencies or organizations. As these are all considered transfers in nature, they are subject to the real estate transfer tax. However, the previous method required the establishment of a contract before the tax could be paid and the ownership could be transferred. The bureau considered that these land transfers were different from ordinary transactions and that requiring a contract would make it difficult to deal with those who delayed establishing contracts. To consolidate tax revenue, new regulations have been established. In the future, for the above-mentioned land transfers, the transfer tax and the additional municipal expenses will be collected based on the transfer evidence, and there will be no need to fill out a contract. The deadline for tax payment will be six months from the date of the transfer, as stipulated in the temporary regulations for collecting real estate transfer tax in this special municipality. Those who exceed the deadline will be penalized according to the regulations. Those who have transferred land before the bureau's announcement but have not yet paid taxes will have one month to pay, and those who exceed the deadline will be handled according to the regulations without further leniency. It is reported that these measures have been approved by the Municipal Land Bureau and filed with the Municipal Government for the record.

Shanghai Businessmen's Readjustment Committee Requests Reiteration of the Order Protecting Human Rights

The Shanghai Businessmen's Readjustment Committee yesterday sent a telegram to the Central Party Headquarters of the National Government regarding the Shanghai Chinese Industry Workers' Union's unauthorized arrest of people, requesting the reiteration of the order protecting human rights. It also sent a letter to the Municipal Civil Training Committee, warning the Workers' Union against falsely claiming secret orders from higher-level agencies to arrest representatives of the drugstore guild. The letters and telegrams are recorded below:

(1) Telegram to the Central Party Headquarters of the Nanjing National Government: We received a letter on the 19th of this month from the Shanghai Special City Pharmaceutical Industry Guild stating, "Previously, the National Government issued a clear order protecting human rights, stating that the freedom of the body of law-abiding merchants and residents should not be infringed upon by others without legal procedures. The Songhu Garrison Command also issued a proclamation prohibiting arbitrary arrests. Unexpectedly, the previous time our guild was forced by the Workers' Union to install unemployed workers, and the representative publicly elected by the guild, Feng Jinpu, and others went to Beijing to petition and returned to Shanghai. Representative Feng cried at the North Station and was accused of being a reactionary by the Workers' Union and arrested by the Public Security Bureau. Our guild has already submitted the above situation to your committee for forwarding to various higher-level agencies for clear explanation. Unexpectedly, at 12:00 noon on the 17th of this month, officials from the Workers' Union rushed into the Yihanchun Drugstore in Xiaodongmen and asked about the manager. When told that the manager was out on business, they arrested the deputy manager without asking any questions and arbitrarily interrogated him at the Pharmaceutical Industry Workers' Union. Although Mr. Song stated that the matter of installing workers had already been submitted to the Central Government for review by the Businessmen's Readjustment Committee and should be resolved, the Pharmaceutical Industry Workers' Union still disregarded the situation and forcibly detained Mr. Song for two hours before releasing him. Such arbitrary arrest of law-abiding citizens is a violation of regulations and laws. We request that your committee forward this matter to various higher-level agencies and severely punish the actions of the Pharmaceutical Industry Workers' Union and reiterate the proclamation protecting human rights to curb the violence and reassure the people." After reviewing the case, it was found that the Public Security Bureau arrested Feng Jinpu at the request of the Workers' Union. The guild had previously reported the matter to the committee, and we were preparing to submit a document requesting the Party and government agencies to investigate and stop it. However, because Feng Jinpu was immediately released on bail, we remained silent. The store sought to resolve the matter in the face of adversity, which is already a clear indication. However, the Workers' Union's illegal actions cannot be resolved through reason. Not many days later, another strange incident of unauthorized arrest occurred. This kind of action not only tramples on the store's rights and disregards human rights, but also treats national laws and regulations as worthless. If this continues for a long time, it will repeat the past events of Wuhan and cause great panic in society. Based on the aforementioned situation, it is reasonable to send a telegram to your government and your department to request a thorough investigation and punishment of the illegal actions of the Workers' Union to warn future offenders and reiterate the order protecting human rights so that everyone is aware of it and unruly elements restrain themselves. This will be in the public interest." (2) Letter from the Municipal Civil Training Committee to the Businessmen's Readjustment Committee: The Secretary's Office forwarded your committee's two official letters dated May 19th and May 20th, which have been received. After investigation, it was found that Representative Feng Jinpu returned to Shanghai after petitioning on behalf of the store and encountered members of the Pharmaceutical Industry Workers' Union at the North Railway Station. The two sides had an argument and twisted each other to the Fifth District Public Security Bureau, where they were released the next day. There is no evidence to prove that they were privately arrested. Song Fuchen accompanied the employees of the Tonghanchun Drugstore to the Social Bureau to petition for mediation regarding the issue of wage demands. The Social Bureau stated that a written request was needed, so they went to the Workers' Union to discuss solutions. There was no evidence of detention or withholding. The guild's exaggerated words are inappropriate, and your committee did not take the time to investigate and hastily made a judgment based on the guild's one-sided statement. It is deeply regrettable. Furthermore, the guild has repeatedly defied orders and refused to negotiate. Such extra-legal actions, as stated in your letter, only serve to increase class antagonism. We hope that your committee will strictly correct them. Otherwise, if this continues for a long time, it will cause great panic in society. This letter is sent to you for your review.

(3) Letter from the Businessmen's Readjustment Committee to the Municipal Civil Training Committee:

Labor-Management Joint Petition for Relief in the Silk and Satin Dyeing Industry

The Shanghai Special Municipality Capital Silk and Satin Dyeing Trade Association, the Labor Shanghai Silk and Satin Dyeing Workers' Union, and the Shanghai Cotton Cloth Dyeing Workers' Union jointly submitted documents to the Bureau of Social Affairs and the Municipal Party Department of the Chamber of Commerce, stating (Labor Side): The petition is submitted because outsiders are taking advantage of the situation to seize and endanger the business, causing various factories to face collapse, and the livelihood of thousands of workers is at stake. We request strict correction to maintain industry regulations and ensure survival. It is true that at the end of the eighteenth year, the association, etc., considering the decline of factory operations and the difficulty of maintaining them, based on the true spirit of labor-management mutual assistance, did not hesitate to sacrifice money and energy to assist the capital side in organizing a dye price consolidation committee in order to save it from its precarious state. After several months of consolidation, considerable results were achieved. Not only were the seventeen factories that had closed down re-established, but also a large number of the hundreds of unemployed workers were placed in jobs. This spirit can be regarded as the pioneer of labor-management cooperation and the beginning of a new era of self-help in various industries. After this, the road ahead was smooth and unimpeded, and labor and management were both bright. However, there are red dye shops that imitate the red dyeing of raw silk, and foreign yuan dye shops that imitate the yuan color dyeing of Japan. In addition, there are silk and satin industry profit-seeking foreign dyeing workers whose purpose is to destroy. These shops see that our industry's dye price consolidation is about to be profitable, so they become covetous and flock to silk shops to arbitrarily cut prices and seize business. For these shops, it is just doing extra business and there is no harm, but for our industry, it is destroying the entire front line and the impact is significant. Now, various factories are facing a precarious situation due to this major blow. The association, etc., is deeply concerned about the situation. The capital side's losses are not to be mentioned for the time being, but what about the livelihood of thousands of workers? Although there are no explicit provisions in our country's commercial scope laws, the old industry regulations have inherent practices that should not be abolished (the Civil Code states that if there are no legal provisions, one can follow custom). Our industry has always had distinctions such as silk and satin, cyan, blue, foreign colors, mercerized printing, red dyeing, finishing, sizing shafts, etc. Recently, foreign yuan dye shops have sprung up, but the business operations are different, the boundaries are clear, and each abides by its scope without any involvement. However, now there are foreign yuan, red dye shops, and this shop that are overstepping their bounds, arbitrarily seizing and cutting dye prices, eliminating alcohol costs, and destroying our industry by any means. This is not a proper business practice. If we do not strictly stop and correct it, then our silk and satin dyeing industry will be fundamentally wiped out, and more than sixty factories will inevitably close down at the same time, and thousands of workers will feel the pain of unemployment. This phenomenon is not exaggerated by the association, etc. The facts are all there and cannot be concealed. Looking at the former second-hand clothing industry and the current pharmaceutical industry, the issue of workers' placement and unemployment has led to disputes. Learning from past events, we have deep-seated concerns. We have always admired your bureau's concern for society and its guarantee of industry and commerce. Therefore, we hereby submit a petition, requesting prompt rescue and strict correction. If there are unscrupulous competitors who intend to seize and destroy, we request that they be stopped and appropriately punished, so as to maintain the old industry regulations and protect industrial and commercial peace and security. Our industry's labor and management will both receive your grace. With utmost sincerity, we submit this petition. (Capital Side) The petition is submitted because outsiders are destroying the business. We request strict orders to stop it in order to ensure business and guarantee capital. The association, etc., is due to the lack of unity among fellow members in previous years, the abandonment of industry regulations, the arbitrary cutting of dye prices, and the different evaluations in the market, resulting in increasingly declining business operations and economic peril. Now, due to the basic erosion, closures are heard from time to time, and the number of unemployed workers is increasing day by day, which affects people's livelihood and is a social concern. The dyeing industry is one of the material cultures of silk and cotton weaving. The rise and fall of business is related to the prosperity and decline of industry and the scarcity of people's livelihood. The Labor Silk and Cotton Dyeing Workers' Union and the Silk and Satin Dyeing Workers' Union deeply understand this. Unwilling to sit idly by, they believe that labor-management cooperation is essential to resolve the crisis. As an essential remedy, they organized a labor-management joint dye price consolidation committee in December of last year to standardize the dye prices of various colors in order to maintain the original capital. All unemployed workers have also been placed in jobs, and substantial subsidies have been properly planned for those who have been unemployed for a long time in order to maintain their livelihoods and avoid repeating the mistakes of the pharmaceutical industry dispute. Unexpectedly, just as the consolidation was underway, a group of miscellaneous outsiders hired foreign workers and intended to disrupt the business by not paying alcohol costs and suppressing dye prices, resulting in the association's price rates being defeated and business being in a state of panic. This kind of overstepping boundaries to seize business, benefit oneself and harm others, aggressively invading business, and deliberately destroying is not only directly destroying the silk and satin dyeing industry, but also indirectly harming the livelihoods of genuine workers. If we do not strictly ban it, the situation will worsen, and the industry affected by the association will inevitably collapse, increasing the number of unemployed workers, disrupting social livelihood, and causing panic and anxiety. Therefore, we have made a list of appeals, earnestly requesting your review and approval, and strictly ordering a stop and taking measures to ban it in order to maintain business and guarantee capital. This will be a great service. We submit this petition with sincerity.

New Procedures for the Bank of China to Collect Checks

Notice to all financial institutions to comply

The Shanghai Bank of China has recently noted that the number of foreign bank checks entrusted by various money shops and Chinese banks is huge, and the number of pages is even greater. Checks are unreliable, and there are often cases of returned checks. Moreover, the returned checks of various banks are often delayed until 6 or 7 pm because the checking procedures are troublesome. The bank needs to spend time and effort to return the checks, and the round trip at night is dangerous. Now, a proper method has been proposed: Checks collected on the same day are not allowed to be used on the same day. In this way, the return of checks can be handled slowly to avoid danger. Therefore, a notice was issued to all financial institutions yesterday, saying: (Respected Sirs, the number of checks entrusted to our bank by various precious shops is very large, and there are bound to be returned checks. The return of checks by various banks is often notified at 6 or 7 o'clock, which is too late, and the procedures are often difficult. Moreover, there are many risks on the way. In the future, please do not use the funds from the checks entrusted to our bank by various precious shops on the same day. Please forgive us and comply. Thank you very much. Shanghai Bank of China, May 31, 1920)

Mr. Zhu Qinglan, Standing Committee Member of the National Government Relief Committee, personally went to the disaster area in Shaanxi to distribute grain and funds. The disaster-stricken people of the Three Qin regions, at this critical moment when their lives depended on breathing, knew they had received a savior. Mr. Sun Weiyi, the representative of the province stationed in Shanghai, received a detailed telegram from Xi'an reporting that Mr. Zhu Qinglan of Beiping arrived in Xi'an at 6 pm. Representatives from the Provincial Relief Committee, Jishi Branch, Red Cross Society, Buddhist Association, and Chinese and Foreign Joint Relief Association greeted him in the suburbs. Those who came with Mr. Zhu included Shang Yunting, Li Zushen, Zhang Huanhai, Tao Fuqing, and Wang Bozhi. In addition, Zhang Xianqing, Jiang Yuntai, and Lu Shuchen, members of the Shanghai Jishi General Association's distribution committee, also arrived in the province at the same time and stayed at the Jiangsu Guild Hall Jishi Branch. After a dinner at 8 pm, various charitable organizations held a welcome meeting at the residence. Deng Changyao, chairman of the Provincial Relief Committee, delivered a welcome speech, and Lu Xiaoyu, president of the Jishi Branch, reported on the general situation of the disaster. Because Mr. Zhu was anxious to provide disaster relief, he immediately asked the groups to discuss relief methods. They all agreed that the disaster was serious during the lean season and that the lives and deaths of the victims were at stake. However, Mr. Zhu's relief grain had not yet arrived, and it was not enough to wait. Mr. Zhu also said that the counties in western Shaanxi were in urgent need of relief, but the cash he brought was limited. He requested the local charitable groups to raise more funds to help. The groups felt that Mr. Song was sincere and immediately undertook to provide more than 200 shi of relief grain, which, together with Mr. Zhu's 800 shi, totaled 1,000 shi, selling for 30,000 yuan in silver. It was decided to distribute the grain in Liquan and Fufeng counties first. The meeting did not end until 1 am the next morning. At 5 am, Mr. Zhu and Li Zushen, etc., took a car back east to transport grain, leaving only Shang Yunting and Zhang Huanhai to distribute urgent relief in Shaanxi. Their enthusiasm and determination are admirable. In addition, Zhang Xianqing, a member of the Shanghai Jishi Association, plans to distribute urgent relief and seeds in Wugong. The disaster relief committee has already set off from the province today.
