The Zhifu Lane Housing Dispute Remains Unresolved

Hibino Opposes Eviction

Greater China Refutes Legally

Since the day Greater China Co., Ltd. purchased the Zhifu Lane property, it has notified each tenant by letter to vacate and return the houses by the end of May for its own use. While this case is being mediated by the Chamber of Commerce by sending letters to each tenant, the Japanese firm Hibino Yoko specially hired attorney Eto Sumi a few days ago to represent the firm in writing to Greater China regarding this lease termination issue, raising objections. Subsequently, Greater China, considering the Japanese firm's letter to be erroneous in its claims, immediately sent a reply to the Japanese representative, severely refuting it. Now, the original letters between the parties involved have been found and are appended below.

Hibino's Letter: Sirs, We are instructed by Hibino Yoko to reply to your esteemed letter of April 30, 19th year of the Republic. Regarding the properties located at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Fujian Road, leased by our clients, the original owner, Dalun Real Estate Co., concluded fixed-term lease contracts with each tenant for a period of twenty years. This contract has been adjudicated by the Shanghai Provisional Court, which confirmed its validity. Therefore, each of our clients, as tenants, still has the right to lease the properties for more than ten years. If it is true that your company has received the land and houses from Dalun Company, your company (as the successor to the rights) can only obtain the rights owned by the former owner (Dalun Company). The successor cannot obtain rights that the former owner did not possess. This is a fundamental principle of law. Therefore, your company's ownership is naturally subject to the restrictions faced by Dalun Company. However, according to the spirit of Article 425 of the Chinese Civil Code (even if the lessor transfers ownership of the leased object to a third party after its delivery, the lease contract continues to exist for the transferee (it is clear that there is such a custom)). Therefore, our clients cannot comply with your company's improper request. Addressed to Greater China Co., Ltd. Respectfully, Attorney Eto Sumi, May 24, 19th year of the Republic of China.

Greater China's Reply: Sirs, We have received and read your letter of the 24th of this month, sent by your esteemed lawyer on behalf of Hibino Yoko. We have already announced that our company has received the property ownership from Dalun Company. The claims made by your advocate on behalf of your client, Hibino Yoko, this time do not conform to the facts or the law. We respectfully state the following points separately: (1) The tenants of the properties located at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Fujian Road, such as Lao Da Fang, have not entered into a fixed-term lease contract for twenty years with Dalun Real Estate Co. This has been clarified and confirmed by the court. The tenants of Lao Da Fang only asserted that there was an oral agreement and provided no evidence. Therefore, the court's judgment on the case included the reasoning that "Regarding the lease of the disputed houses by the appellant (referring to Dalun Company), if there were agreed terms, as with the former tenant of Mao Fu Hao (i.e., the Nanyang Socks Factory) and the appellant Hua Ying Pharmacy (fixed term of six years, already expired), written contracts were signed. If other tenants had also agreed to a term of twenty years, why would there be no written record? Furthermore, why would the appellants (referring to Lao Da Fang, etc.) willingly increase the rent beyond the original amount of more than 60,000 taels per year, willingly adding 40,000 taels to cancel the exchange condition of reclaiming the houses? The claim of an oral agreement for a term of twenty years is not credible." This was used to refute the reasons of Lao Da Fang, etc. This judgment has long been published by the court, and all newspapers have carried it. Furthermore, referring to Article 422 of the Chinese Civil Code (a lease contract for real estate with a term of more than one year should be made in writing; if not made in writing, it is regarded as a lease without a fixed term), this further proves that the so-called oral agreement for a term of twenty years absolutely cannot exist. We believe that your esteemed advocate, once attentive to reviewing, will be able to fully understand this. (2) Article 450 of the Chinese Civil Code stipulates that "If a lease has a fixed term, the lease relationship terminates when the term expires. If there is no fixed term, each party may terminate the contract at any time." The lease relationship between your client and each tenant with the former owner, Dalun Company, is not a fixed-term lease contract, but a lease contract without a fixed term, as previously stated. According to the aforementioned law, the provision for termination of the contract at any time should be absolutely applied. Your esteemed advocate is well-versed in the law and should be able to convey to your client to act in accordance with the law, so as not to regard a lease without a fixed term as a perpetual lease. (3) All leases without a fixed term are clearly stated in the house ticket: such as, if one party wishes to terminate the contract, both parties must give notice of termination within a period of one month. This is not only a common practice in Shanghai and other places, but it can also be considered a special agreement mutually recognized by both parties. The terms recorded on the house ticket are the expression of intent by the owner (i.e., the lessor), and all house tickets are delivered to the tenant (i.e., the lessee) for safekeeping. There is no doubt that the tenant tacitly approves of the terms recorded on the house ticket. According to contract principles, any evidence of mutual agreement between the parties, whether express or implied, can be considered as a valid contract (refer

Page 16

ence (2) The tenant is in arrears with rent for three months. (3) The house is damaged and requires reconstruction before it can be vacated, etc. Regardless of whether the claim is appropriate, the court also relies on this as the basis for its judgment. Whether, according to the claim put forward by the tenant, the company's intention to reclaim the house for its own use should be considered in accordance with this custom is undoubtedly. Based on the above, we request your esteemed advocate to convey to your client that you still hope to comply with our company's previous notice to vacate within the time limit, in order to comply with the spirit of a country ruled by law where people abide by the law. Sincerely, To Japanese Attorney Eto Sumi, the 28th day of the fifth month, 19th year of the Republic.

Shanghai Municipal Council Cracks Down on Excessive Use of Car Horns

Traffic Superintendent Issues Special Warning

Traffic Superintendent of the Shanghai Municipal Council Police Department announces: Car owners should be aware that the sound of car horns is causing public nuisance. Please pay special attention to Article 30 of the Traffic Regulations: Drivers are not allowed to use horns, bells, or other warning devices unnecessarily to avoid public annoyance. Please also note and warn your drivers that the police are determined to severely punish those who violate this regulation in the future. Special warning: Under the following circumstances, there is no need to use the horn: (1) In residential areas from 11:00 PM to 6:00 AM. (2) At any time, anywhere, or under any circumstances, unless one is genuinely obstructed and there is a risk of danger to pedestrians or other vehicles, and unless such obstruction cannot be avoided even by reducing speed (in such cases, one or two short sounds are sufficient; long or continuous sounds are prohibited). (3) In front of any house, using the horn as a warning to people inside. (4) On deserted and sparsely trafficked roads. (5) To maintain or increase vehicle speed. Vehicles equipped with squeeze bulb horns do not need to use electric horns unless absolutely necessary. If drivers operate vehicles in accordance with Articles 20 and 21 of the Traffic Regulations, they will not only reduce the number of times they need to use the horn, but also reduce the chance of causing trouble. All Traffic Regulations can be obtained in person or by mail from the Traffic Office free of charge. Issued by the Traffic Superintendent of the Shanghai Municipal Council Police Department, May 29, 1930.

Humorous Account of a Wife Concealment Case

A Wealthy Family's Maid Becomes a Villager's Wife

Twice Married, Suddenly Disappears

The First Precinct of the Second District of the city yesterday received a case reported by Ding Fusheng from Suzhou, along with his fellow villagers Wu Aqian and Pu Genfu, accusing someone of concealing his wife. The content is quite humorous. There is a Zhang mansion in Suzhou city.

There are many maids, and they are sent away to marry when they reach adulthood, but a small amount of betrothal money is collected. Among them, there is a maid named A'da, who is eighteen years old this year, and was bought in since childhood. Her surname is still unknown.

She is quite beautiful. Pu, a villager from Hu Shu Pass, Pu Genfu's mother, often works as a helper in the city. She knew that the Zhang mansion wanted to send the maid away to marry.

Being eager for a grandson and lacking large sums to complete the marriage for Genfu, she considered this cheap option and bought A'da for 130 yuan the year before last, completing the marriage for her son and forming a family. After marriage, the maid, who grew up in

a wealthy family, although her status was low, did not have to endure the hardships of rural life, and thought highly of herself, disdaining

to associate with rural laborers, and was often dissatisfied with her family, leading to discord. Moreover, Pu Genfu liked to gamble and gambled heavily during the Lunar New Year last year, incurring substantial losses and debt, which he could not repay, resulting in the

intention to sell his wife. About three miles from Pu's house, there is a farmer named Ding Fusheng, 30 years old, living with his mother. His family has several acres of farmland, sufficient for self-sufficiency in the village, and no extra money to marry a wife, so although he is of marriageable age,

his marriage is still vacant. His mother heard that Pu Genfu intended to sell his wife, which was a perfect match for her son, so they agreed on a betrothal gift of 220 yuan, mortgaged the farmland, and obtained the money to go to A'da's house on the twelfth day of the first month

to become his new bride. However, Ding's family is of the same type as Pu's, and the hardship of her labor is still the same. Moreover, Ding's appearance is not as good as Pu's, so A'da became even more dissatisfied. However, Ding treated A'da

as a celestial being and flattered her in every way, so she reluctantly lived with him for one year and three months. On May 19th of this year, she secretly fled without a trace. After losing his wife, Ding Fusheng was greatly alarmed, fearing

both loss of money and person, so he searched everywhere but found nothing. Later, a letter was sent from Wu Aqian, a fellow villager living at No. 11 Dajilu, Huangjiaque Road, Ximen, Shanghai, stating that A'da had been there on the 20th. At that time, Ding was not at home. When he returned home and saw the letter, he rushed to Wu's house, but A'da

had suddenly disappeared again. When asked, Wu Aqian said that A'da stayed for three days and then left, saying that she was going to Pu Genfu's place. Ding inquired about Pu's address, and was told that it was at the

Red Rail Bridge Shanghai Candy Company. He went to find Pu and was denied meeting A'da. Ding, in desperation, argued that Wu Aqian and A'da did not know each other, so how could she stay at his house, clearly colluding with Pu to hide her, so he called the police and arrested them. The First Precinct of the Second District immediately transferred them to the District Court for verification.

Forcibly Kissing

A Tailor's Vexatious Behavior

Wang Guiren's Daughter Assaulted

Wang Guiren, a native of Changzhou residing at No. 6 Dexing Lane, Xinmin Road, Zhabei, works as a chef and has a daughter named Lindi, who is of marriageable age and quite beautiful. She currently works in a nearby silk factory. Shao Xing tailors Ji Awu, Ji Ali, and Sheng Tai, who live on the same road in Fengxiang Lane, arbitrarily tease and ridicule Lindi every evening when she passes by the alley entrance after work. Lindi is taciturn and ignores them. Awu and others think Lindi can be bullied. The previous night, at around 8:00 PM, Lindi went out to buy things and passed by the same place again. Awu and others went forward and grabbed Lindi's hand, intending to kiss her. Lindi became enraged and cursed loudly, and Awu and others also cursed back. As they argued, Lindi went home and tearfully told her father what had happened. Wang then went to reason with them, but Awu and others were not there. Unexpectedly, at 7:30 AM yesterday morning, Awu and others gathered many hooligans and went to Lindi's house, dragging her father, Wang Guiren, into the alley and brutally beating him, causing Wang's head to be broken and bleeding profusely, causing serious injuries. Seeing that they had caused a major disaster, Awu and others took the opportunity to escape. The patrol police arrived and took the landlady of the tailor shop to the First Precinct of the Fourth District to hand over Awu and others for investigation.

Grand-Aunt and Grand-Nephew

An Incestuous Elopement Case

Chen Wangshi, the wife of Chen Rurong, a laborer from Funing, living at No. 48 Zhangjiabang Road, Pudong, is 31 years old this year. However, this woman is naturally licentious. Chen Rurong has a direct cousin, Chen Deli, 33 years old, living at No. 33 on the same street, who often goes to his grand-uncle's house. Chen Wangshi, regardless of seniority, immediately developed affection for her grand-nephew upon seeing his strength, so they exchanged amorous glances, and Chen Deli was, of course, perceptive. Thus, they engaged in an animalistic act that greatly altered human ethics. Moreover, since they could not do as they pleased, they eloped to Dalianwan Road on May 1st to the house of Deli's brother, Demu. The grand-aunt and grand-nephew actually became husband and wife. After his wife fled, Chen Rurong began to inquire and learned that his wife was at Demu's place, so he filed a complaint with the Third Precinct of the Third District yesterday. The police dispatched officers to arrest Chen Deli and Chen Wangshi together. The case involves incest and was immediately transferred to the District Court for interrogation.

Verdict in the Shanghai West Major Gambling Case

The Shanghai West Connaught Road roulette gambling case was heard yesterday afternoon by Judge Nian and Prosecutor Liu. The manager of the gambling den, Zhang Jinbao (aka Wang Shoutang), was found guilty of operating a gambling den for profit, illegally possessing firearms without government permission, and illegally possessing opium paraphernalia. Prohibition of Cargo Vehicles Passing Through Hengfeng Bridge

Traffic Diverted to Wuzhen Bridge

After the southern section of the Hengfeng Bridge in Zhabei collapsed in 1927, a temporary wooden bridge was rebuilt by the Municipal Works Bureau, with the contractor guaranteeing its stability for three years. Now that the guarantee period is about to expire, the bureau has sent personnel to inspect the bridge and found that the two rows of piles in the northern section, the part that did not collapse at the time, are severely corroded. Repairs are currently being planned. Before the repairs are completed, it is stipulated that small cars, rickshaws, passenger cars, and empty cargo trucks can still pass as usual. All trucks and dump trucks carrying cargo are prohibited from passing through the bridge and must be diverted to Wuzhen Bridge to avoid danger. It is reported that the Municipal Works Bureau has erected signs on the bridge and has sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau to instruct the police officers in that area to pay attention to and crack down on violations at any time.

Dispute over French Concession Police Expelling Street Vendors

Xujiahui Town in Shanghai West is located at the intersection of the Chinese and French territories. Due to its strategic location, the French Concession has established a police booth at the Zhaojiabang Bridge to station Chinese and Vietnamese police officers to prevent any emergencies. Xujiahui Town is the leading town in Shanghai West, with a gathering of merchants and civilians. However, there is no proper vegetable market, so before 9:00 AM, villagers carry vegetable baskets on their shoulders and set up stalls on both sides of the road to sell their goods. However, the French Concession No. 145 Chinese police officer Yang Rongsheng (20 years old, from Yancheng, newly appointed as a patrol officer) drove away all the small vegetable stalls around the turn of the Bédan Road on the 29th (yesterday morning) and kicked over the vegetable baskets at will, leaving the poor vendors in dire straits. The vendors moved to the Chinese territory in droves, causing temporary disorder. Zhao Xiwun, the second patrol officer of the Sixth Precinct of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, Sixth District, witnessed the situation and quickly stopped him. The Chinese police officer reported to the Shanzhong Road police station, which sent three officers to inquire. The acting patrol officer, Xue Jinxian, informed the three officers that the police officer had expelled the vegetable vendors. The three officers publicly reprimanded the Chinese police officer, and then they dispersed. Unexpectedly, after being reprimanded, the police officer became angry and, together with Chinese police officer No. 623, sought trouble with police officer Xie Yongzhang of the Third Patrol. Without asking why, they seized Xie's police equipment and forcibly dragged him to the French Concession. Fortunately, Xie was quick-witted and immediately sounded the whistle for help. At that time, the onlookers were indignant and helped the police officer to arrest the two Chinese police officers and bring them back to the station. Soon, Gu Laike (transliteration), the deputy police chief of Shanzhong Road, arrived to request bail. Director Xu of the Xujiahui Police Station reported the matter by telephone to Director Yuan, as the case was of great importance. Director Yuan instructed the two Chinese police officers who had caused the trouble to be handed over to the police chief to be severely punished to maintain friendship, etc. Director Xu told him the details of the incident and allowed him to take them back first, while preparing a document to report to Director Yuan and request serious negotiations with the French Consul to safeguard sovereignty and avoid disputes.

Mother Grieves Over Daughter's Abduction and Commits Suicide

An elderly woman from Jiangbei, Xiao Li, 55 years old, lives in a grass shed near Xiangyanqiao, Zhabei. She has a daughter named Jinlian, who is ten years old and quite beautiful. Her neighbor, Miao Xiaoyuan, from Yancheng, works as a dockworker and, seeing Jinlian's beauty, seduced her and committed adultery. A month ago, they both eloped. Xu Zhiren, who lives with her, said to Xiao Li yesterday, "Your daughter was abducted by Miao, I know it very well. If you go abroad and seek blessings, you can recover her." Xiao Li loved her daughter very much. Now that Xu knew where she was, she might as well go and look for her together. If she could get her daughter back, she would respect him with five Buddha statues. Xu then firmly said that it was impossible and angrily walked away. Xiao Li still wanted to hold his hand, but Xu was strong and Xiao fell to the ground. After a while, the woman, feeling that life was meaningless, committed suicide at 3:00 PM by cutting her throat with a vegetable knife, exposing her trachea. Later, her neighbor took her to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but because the cut was very deep, it was feared that she could not be saved. However, the incident was caused by a slip of the tongue by Xu Zhiren, and he has now been detained by the Third Precinct of the Fifth District.

Angrily Killing a Beloved Wife

Married for Over a Decade

Giving Way to Impulse

Dong, a Native of the Mao Family, is in Critical Condition

Mao Gengyang, a native of Ningbo, is 30 years old and lives at No. 47 Wangshan Lane, Zhoushan Road. He usually sells beef for a living. His wife, Dong, is also 30 years old, also from Ningbo, and has a son named Qiankang, who is just 14 years old. They are usually very harmonious. Unexpectedly, at noon yesterday, the couple suddenly had an argument for unknown reasons, and Mao Gengyang took a beef knife and stabbed his wife Dong in the left chest. Dong collapsed to the ground in pain. Seeing that he had caused a disaster, Mao immediately took her to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but her injuries were very critical and she has been transferred to Guangren Hospital for treatment. It is said that her intestines are severed and it is difficult to save her, and her life is feared to be in danger.

Patrol Police Arrest Gun-Carrying Criminal Mid-Patrol

Sighting Four Suspicious Men

Chasing and Capturing Qiang Haosheng

Patrol police Zhu Lianqing, Xu Fuzhou, Jin Jiushan, and Li Furen of the First Precinct of the Nanshi District were patrolling at around 8:00 AM yesterday when they saw four men get off the No. 1 streetcar of the Huashang Tram Company, traveling from Xiaodongmen to Dongsheng Road. After alighting, they walked south, behaving very suspiciously. Since they were already far away, the police officers jumped on the streetcar and chased after them. When they reached the Merchants' Guild Wharf, they saw only three people. One person was missing. Seeing the urgency, Policeman Zhu immediately got out of the car and grabbed a man. After a brief search, nothing was found, and he was released. The man then ran away in a hurry, making him even more suspicious. Policeman Zhu immediately ordered Policeman Xu and others to catch up and arrest him. He then approached the two men and grabbed them with both hands, ordering them to stop. As he was about to conduct a search, one of them pulled out a pistol from his pocket and aimed it at Policeman Zhu's temple, intending to fire. For some reason, the bullet did not come out. Policeman Zhu glanced back and saw the pistol. Having no choice, he released the man he was holding and pulled out his own pistol, intending to resist. Since there were many onlookers on the road, the man fled into the crowd and disappeared without a trace. Policeman Zhu was afraid that the other man he was holding would also escape, so he did not chase after him and brought the man back to the station. One of the men chased by Policeman Xu and others ran straight to Luxi Street. In a panic, the man pulled out a pistol from his pants and fired four shots backwards. Fortunately, they did not hit anyone. When the bullets ran out, he threw the pistol aside and fled into a small alley. The police officers picked up the pistol he had dropped and took it back to the station. After reporting the matter to the station chief, he brought the man Zhu arrested for preliminary interrogation. According to his confession, his name is Qiang Haosheng, 23 years old, from Wuxi, and he works as a clerk in Qiang Dechang Western Iron Shop at No. 55 Noxin Road, Datong Road. Today, a friend Wu Achun (referring to one of those who escaped) invited me to work together at the wharf. I didn't know he had a pistol in his bag, etc. He was ordered to be temporarily detained for investigation and further verification.

The Tragic Death of Li Lian

Assassination or Robbery?

Li's Wife Weeps Bitterly

Hong Benli, the former magistrate of Fengxian County, came to Shanghai after resigning and lived at No. 1107 and a half, Chuanfuli, Xinzha Road, for half a month. His secretary, Li Lian, also lived in Hong's residence in the rear room on the upper floor. On the morning of the 29th of last month, four bandits suddenly broke into Hong's house. One bandit with a pistol went upstairs. Li shouted wildly when he saw them, and the bandit fired two shots, hitting Li's vital organs, and he fell to the ground and died. The four bandits then fled together. After the case occurred, some suspected it was an assassination, and others suspected it was a robbery because Li's shouting led to him being shot. The police station in charge sent detectives to investigate and transported the body to the Fellen Road autopsy center. The next morning, Prosecutor Guo, commissioned by the Special District Court, arrived at the center to conduct an autopsy. The wife of the deceased cried until her tears ran dry, pleading for the arrest of the murderer to bring justice. Hong also appeared in the case and stated that he was willing to take charge of the burial because the family of the deceased was poor and unable to purchase clothes and a coffin. Prosecutor Guo then ordered the corpse to be handed over to Hong Benli for burial.

Wang Ajin Shot to Death by Bandits

At around 10:00 AM, Wang Ajin, residing at No. 68 Xiaoshadu Road, went out with his friend Wu Lirong. Just as they reached the entrance, Wang stopped to urinate. Suddenly, four bandits appeared, pulled out pistols, and shot at Wang. Wu quickly turned around and ran into the house unscathed. Wang was hit by a bullet and fell into a pool of blood. When the Putuo Road police station in charge received the report, they sent detectives to the scene, but the two murderers were nowhere to be seen. Wang had already died, and his body was transported to the Fellen Road autopsy center. Yesterday, Prosecutor Guo, commissioned by the Special District Court, arrived at the center to conduct an autopsy and ordered the corpse to be taken for burial by the wife of the deceased, Wang Ding.

70,000 Red Pills Found in a Rickshaw

Yesterday morning around three o'clock, a rickshaw with the license number 5701 from the concession, passing the entrance of Lanting Lane on Hengfeng Road in Zhabei, was being pulled northward by a rickshaw puller. Wan Qi, from the fourth guardhouse of the second precinct of the fourth district, noticed that although the rickshaw was empty, the rickshaw puller looked flustered, as if carrying heavy items. He immediately went forward to search, initially finding nothing. However, upon removing the cushion, he was greatly shocked to discover a large quantity of red pills, totaling seventy boxes with 70,000 pills. The rickshaw puller and the red pills were taken to the precinct. After questioning by Director Li, the rickshaw puller confessed that he was Wu Hongtu, a 21-year-old from Yancheng, residing at Yaojia Stone Bridge on Xinmin Road. He said that earlier, he had been pulling his rickshaw to Taiping Bridge on Caishi Street in the French Concession when two well-dressed individuals asked him to transport the items to the Maigen Road station. They placed the items inside the cushion, with one person sitting on the rickshaw and the other following behind. When they reached Hengfeng Bridge, the person in the rickshaw suddenly got off, instructing him to pull the rickshaw ahead, and he claimed to have no knowledge that the contents were contraband. Director Li, noting that the rickshaw puller's clothing was neat and that his story was suspicious, suspected him of being involved in trafficking, despite his evasive statements, and ordered him to be sent to the bureau for further investigation.

Liang Lianzhi Sues Her Husband for Cohabitation

And Demands Alimony Supplement

A woman named Liang Lianzhi, originally from Zhongshan, Guangdong, is 26 years old. On February 24th, 1925, she married Xie Zhaogui, from the same hometown, through a matchmaker. At that time, Xie was working at Butterfield & Swire (太古洋行), earning a substantial monthly income. On December 18th of the same year, Liang gave birth to a daughter. Xie, having had an affair, did not have a strong relationship with his wife. Even when he occasionally returned home, he only inquired about his elderly father, ignoring Liang. In April 1928, after the death of Xie's father, Xie, no longer restrained, leased out the house and moved all the furniture to 905 Weihai Lane (衛海里), Weihaiwei Road, permanently cohabitating with his mistress and abandoning Liang. Liang was left with no choice but to take her daughter and live at her sister's house at 13 Fudeli (輔德里), Baochang Road, Zhabei. One day, Xie suddenly invited Liang to the accounting firm of Wang Zikang (王梓康) (which also had a lawyer's sign), attempting to force her to sign a divorce agreement. Liang saw through the plan, and Xie's scheme failed. Later, mutual friends, feeling sorry for Liang's loneliness, mediated, and Xie reluctantly agreed to pay her 50 yuan in alimony each month. The payment was handled by Wu Fozhong (吳茀仲), a Cantonese working at Jardine Matheson (怡和洋行). However, after only three months, the payments stopped. From December 1928 to May of this year, Liang has been living on borrowed money, accumulating significant debt. Her plight as an abandoned wife is truly pitiful. She has been forced to seek legal assistance, retaining lawyer Zhang Deqin (張德欽) to file a lawsuit in the Special District Court against Xie Zhao, demanding cohabitation and requesting 950 yuan to cover 19 months of unpaid alimony. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhou Daren (周逹仁) opened the court, summoning the plaintiff, Xie Liang Lianzhi, who arrived with her five-year-old daughter and lawyer Zhang, to recount her abandonment. Her face was filled with sorrow, and tears almost welled up in her eyes. However, her daughter was jumping around in front of her mother, displaying a state of innocent happiness. If Xie could see this, perhaps it would stir feelings for his child. Unfortunately, Xie, fearful of appearing in court, did not come in person and appointed lawyer Ni Jiong (倪炯) to represent him. After questioning, Judge Zhou determined that further witness testimony was needed and adjourned the hearing to 10:00 AM on June 2nd.

Fish Market Dispute Case Verdict

Zhang and Shui Fined and Released

Chen and Wang Imprisoned for One Month, Permitted to Pay to Redeem

Zhang Zhisheng (張志勝) and Shui Jiakuan (水嘉寛), managers of the Fukang Fish Market (福康魚行) outside the Xiaodongmen Bund in the French Concession, had, last month, unsuccessfully attempted to encroach on the stall space of the neighboring Qianfeng Fish Market (乾豐魚行). They gathered dozens of associates from Fukang, Yuantong (源通), and Taichang (泰昌) fish markets, including Chen Aqing (陳阿青) and Wang Ashuang (王阿雙), and led them to the Qianfeng Market, where they beat and injured eight associates, including Wang Mingyuan (王明元), Yan Zuying (嚴祖英), and Liu Zhusheng (劉竹生). Subsequently, Wang Mingyuan and others from Qianfeng Fish Market retained lawyer Bao He (包和) to file a lawsuit in the French Concession Court, accusing the defendants Zhang Zhisheng and Shui Jiakuan of acting barbarously and violating criminal law, requesting strict punishment according to the law, and seeking compensation of 299 yuan for medical expenses and over 400 yuan for all losses. The defendants also retained a lawyer to defend them. After hearing the case, the court adjourned to await the verdict. Yesterday, the verdict was announced. The prosecutor's office summoned both parties, and Judge Zhu (朱承審官) ruled that the case was based on a dispute between parties in the same trade. The defendants Zhang Zhisheng and Shui Jiakuan should not have gathered a crowd to assault the plaintiffs and damage their goods, which violated criminal law. Zhang and Shui were each fined 25 yuan, and Chen Aqing and Wang Ashuang were each sentenced to one month of imprisonment, with the option to pay to redeem their sentences, to serve as a warning. The defendants were ordered not to harass the plaintiffs again. The medical expenses were to be borne two-thirds by the defendants Zhang, and they were to bear one-fifth of the losses. This is the verdict.

Shanghai Bank Adds Two More Branches

At Xiaodongmen and Tilanqiao

The Shanghai Bank's reputation for creditworthiness and business development has long been praised by the Chinese people. The bank has already established branches in Hongkou, Jielu, and Ximen. This summer, it has added another branch on Jing'an Temple Road, forming four branches in the east, west, north, and south. Hongkou is in the east, Jielu in the north, Ximen in the south, and Jing'an Temple Road in the west, naturally forming the boundaries in the four directions. Now, two more branches have been added at Xiaodongmen and Tilanqiao. The manager of the Xiaodongmen branch has been appointed as Wu Shaoting (吳少亭), the manager of the Ximen branch, who has been transferred from the head office. The manager of the Tilanqiao branch has been appointed as Xi Jigeng (奚季耕), who has been transferred from the head office. The position of manager of the Ximen branch has been filled by Ying Jianfu (應儉甫) from the head office. Ying has a deep reputation in the banking industry. During the late Qing dynasty, he worked at the Yu Su Guan Qian Ju (裕蘇官錢局) with excellent results. In 1912, when Chen Guangfu (陳光甫) founded the Jiangsu Bank (江蘇銀行), Ying worked at the bank for eight years. After Chen founded the Shanghai Bank, he invited Ying to take charge of cashier and business operations. Over the past ten years, he has provided significant assistance. Now, he has been transferred to be the manager of the branch, allowing Ying to use his twenty years of experience to develop his strengths. It is believed that the business will improve day by day. It is reported that Ying will go to the Ximen branch on June 2nd to take office.

Bi Yutang's Lawsuit for Being Killed by a Foreigner's Car

On the morning of May 26th, at 8:30 AM, Bi Yutang (畢毓棠), a native of Lanxi, Zhejiang, was walking north at the intersection of Xizang Road and Nanjing Road when he was struck by a bicycle driven by Pollonetsky (博隆尼士基), a Polish man. He fell to the ground and was taken to Tongren Hospital by ambulance, but he died. On the 28th, the Special District Court appointed prosecutor Guo Huaipu (郭懷璞) to examine the body at Linglun Road. The examination found that the corpse's left leg was crushed and the bone was broken, confirming that he had been killed by a car. Bi was 61 years old and worked as a clerk at the Huichun Opium Cessation Bureau (回春戒烟局) on Baker Road. He has one son who is a postman. After his death, his family is in a dire situation. Lawyer Zhao Chen (趙琛) has volunteered to provide legal assistance and has filed a lawsuit according to the law.

Introduction (Newly Compiled Prescriptions)

(Newly Compiled Prescriptions) written by Japanese medical doctors Kuroyu Masae (黑由昌惠) and Honda Yoshitaro (本多芳太郎) has been reprinted ten times in eight years, selling tens of thousands of copies. It has now been translated into Chinese by local doctor Zhang Kecheng (張克成) from the latest edition and will be published. The pre-order price for one month is two yuan, with a postal fee of two jiao. It is distributed by the Life Hospital (生活醫院) on Baille Road. It is reported that the book is finely printed on Daolin paper, hardbound, and contains a total of 400,000 words. Since the start of pre-sales a week ago, more than a hundred copies have been pre-ordered by medical universities and practicing doctors both locally and externally.

China Travel Service Establishes a West Shanghai Branch

The China Travel Service head office has recently opened a branch office inside the Shanghai Bank branch at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Tongfu Road to facilitate travel for merchants and residents in West Shanghai, where the number of shops and households has increased. It began operations on the 26th of last month and is operating as usual today.

New Building of the Chinese Independent Church Completed

In accordance with the principle of abolishing unequal treaties, the Chinese Jesus Church Independent Headquarters has entirely purchased a base with Chinese funds and built a church building on Xiangyin Road in North Shanghai. The building has been completed, and the dedication ceremony is scheduled for June 1st. The department has continuously received gifts, including a large-print Bible purchased for the veterans' hall, a mirror plaque from Huai'en Hall (懷恩堂) and the editor of Tong Wen Bao (通問報) Chen Chunsheng (陳春生), and another from the committee of the Sichuan Bao Merchants Association Zhang Jiongrong (張炯榮), which are on display.

Student Yin Maozhao of the Shanghai Art School Dies Suddenly

Yin Maozhao (陰懋昭), a student from Luxian (瀘縣), Sichuan Province, in the Chinese painting department of the Shanghai Art School, rented a room on the upper floor of the Yixingtai (義興泰) tobacco and paper shop at 441 Caishi Road in the French Concession for only two months. He suddenly died of illness around 5:00 AM on the morning of the 29th of last month. His roommate and fellow townsman, Jiang, immediately discovered it and reported to other students at the Art School, requesting the school authorities to assist with the funeral arrangements. Consequently, the school's director of general affairs, Ding Yuanli (丁遠立), issued a notice to collect funeral expenses from all faculty and students. At the same time, he immediately notified the French police station to investigate and verify the cause of death. The school then handed over all the donated funds to several representatives from the student's hometown, who immediately rushed to make arrangements for the coffin to be placed at 4:30 PM that afternoon.

Lost Mute Boy Waiting to Be Claimed

The Municipal Public Security Bureau sent a lost mute boy from the second station of the sixth district yesterday. His name, age, and family situation are unknown. The child has a shaven head and multiple scars on the back of his head. He is wearing an ant-patterned single shirt and pants, with a white small vest underneath, barefoot. He has 14 incense tablets and two film threads in his pocket. The child has been temporarily sent to the Xin Puyu Tang (新普育堂) for care, waiting to be claimed.

Acknowledgement: We thank the Commercial Press for the donation of the Oriental Magazine, Volume 27, Number 1, and the Children's World, Volume 25, Numbers 10, 12, and 13. Thank you.

Correction: Regarding the news item "The Shandong Jinan Silk Industry Association Cautiously Releases Funds After Deliberation" published on the 30th, the Shandong Jinan Silk Industry Association has sent a letter stating that the industry did not meet on the 29th. We apologize for the error.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast for yesterday at 4:30 PM was: Hot weather with southwest winds north of Shandong. Winds south of Shandong will be favorable and very directionless. The wind is moving slowly over the north of Miyako Island, which will cause cyclones and severe weather in the north and south of the East Sea and as far as the central Chinese coast. Also, the temperature in the city during the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was a high of 84.5 and a low of 70.5. The same day last year had a high of 86.9 and a low of 59.2.

China Ranks Second Overall Due to Volleyball Victory

The Nation Is Heartbroken Over Not Winning the Soccer Championship

We Hope the Citizens Will Come Together to Avenge This Shame

History of China's Failed Soccer Negotiations

Resolution After Match: Title Reserved

China Protests Again the Next Day

Unexpectedly, Japan Insists on Previous Agreement

What's Done Is Done, Nothing Can Be Done

Our Country Strongly Requests Continued Competition with a Different, Fair Referee

Japan Answers That the Day's Referee Is the Most Competent in Japan

Overseas Chinese Are Extremely Angry and Request Withdrawal from the Games

Both China and Japan Ranked First to搪塞

All Chinese Athletes

This Newspaper's May 31st, Tokyo Telegram

After the soccer competition ended in a tie, our country's representatives held an emergency meeting regarding Japan's attitude on the 30th. Afterwards, they officially negotiated with senior Japanese officials, requesting a continuation of the match to determine who should win the championship. However, the Japanese insisted that after the game on the 29th, the coaches immediately held a meeting and unanimously agreed that there was no need for another game to determine the winner. Therefore, the negotiation was unsuccessful. However, afterwards, according to our country's soccer coach, he had stated to the Japanese side that this matter was important and needed to be approved by our country's delegation's executive committee. However, the Japanese misunderstood and, after a heated debate, Japan still insisted on the same agreement and refused to concede, ultimately leading to the decision that the soccer championship would be reserved for the next competition. Both China and Japan would each receive first-place medals for this competition. According to this complex content, the reporter also heard that our country's committee initially proposed a rematch, with the condition that another fair and capable referee be used. However, the Japanese said that the referee that day was already the most competent in Japan. Therefore, the negotiation had no results. In fact, to put it bluntly, even if the referee could be replaced and the game replayed, our country might not necessarily be able to win. Because the new referee could still declare our players offside when they had an attack or a good opportunity. If our players had any rash actions, their qualifications could be revoked. In short, they would do anything and everything to ruin our chances of winning.

Overseas Chinese Enraged

This Newspaper's May 31st, Tokyo Telegram: After the soccer match on the 29th, hundreds of our country's students who were cheerleaders were angry at the referee's unfairness and remained in the stands, refusing to leave. Three representatives were pushed forward to see the coaches and officials, demanding withdrawal from the games, strongly protesting the Japanese referee's bias. Finally, Hao Boyang (郝伯陽) came forward to comfort them, asking the cheerleaders to restrain themselves slightly and maintain national dignity. There were still several students who were filled with anger, scolding the delegation's weakness, uselessness, and loss of national dignity. After some time, the cheerleaders saw that continued resistance was useless and left with anger.

Zhang Boling Negotiates Again

Associated Press, May 31st, Tokyo: Regarding the soccer championship dispute at the Far Eastern Games, the Chinese and Japanese representatives discussed the results on the 29th and decided to reserve the decision, which would be formally decided by the Games' general affairs committee on the 30th. However, at 10:00 AM yesterday morning, China suddenly requested a rematch in the name of Zhang Boling. Therefore, the representatives from both sides negotiated again, and the results were announced as follows. The general affairs committee's decision was resolved.

The general affairs committee of the Ninth Far Eastern Games recognizes that the China-Japan soccer match on the 29th was a tie. Because the Games' dates have expired, there will be no rematch. The championship trophy will be reserved until the next games, and the soccer silver cup will be kept by the Philippines, the organizer of the next games. Both China and Japan will be ranked first.

Resolutions of the General Affairs Meeting

The world rules will be adopted for the next competition

Athletics will be divided into three championships: track and field and all-around

Tennis will use Davis Cup rules

If the soccer is a tie, the time will be extended, and the referee will be from a third country. China has already suffered a loss this year

Other ball game matches must be decided. The rules for baseball will be changed, and swimming events will also be changed

Next Games in the Philippines in 1934

The Philippines proposed the third week of May for a start date, China proposed August. The issue will be considered later.

New Officials Elected: President, Philippines, Quezon

Honorary President, Kishi Seiichi; First President, Wang Zhengting; Second President, Fan Jiasi

The regulatory commission has not yet resolved amateur sports rules

The above resolutions are more detrimental than beneficial to China and should be heeded

This Newspaper, May 29th, Tokyo: The General Affairs Committee of the Far Eastern Games held a meeting on the morning of May 29th. Important committees from China, Japan, the Philippines, and India attended to discuss the draft rules submitted by the Regulatory Commission. Subsequently, the following resolutions were passed:

(1) Starting from the next games, the athletics competition will be divided into three championships: track events, field events, and all-around competitions. World rules will be applied. The discus throw will be considered by communication later. The scoring for the pentathlon and decathlon will be considered by the subcommittee.

(2) The swimming events for the next games will be divided into 50-meter, 100-meter, 400-meter, and 2,500-meter freestyle swimming, 100-meter backstroke, 200-meter breaststroke, and 100-meter relay. The 200-meter relay will be cancelled.

(3) If the participating countries cannot agree on the section without a final match, it is resolved that if it is not decided in advance not to have a final, the final must be forcibly held to determine the championship.

(4) If the result of the soccer match is a tie, the game time should be extended.

Games Flag

The letters FEAA cleverly form a pattern in the flag. The pattern will be used as a symbol on all game certificates and documents.

(5) All ball game officials, especially referees, should be invited to be neutral parties who have no relationship with the ball game to avoid unpleasant disputes.

(6) Tennis will now be called lawn tennis Lawn Tawn Tennis. For competitions with eight or fewer players, Davis Cup rules will be applied. The championship country from the previous games will also join the draw to eliminate priority rights. The distribution of eight players is as follows: four singles players and four doubles players.

(7) Those who join baseball should be under 20 years old. American Major League rules will be applied. The referee officials used in each game should be agreed upon by both sides.

(8) The Indian representative proposed listing hockey as a competition item. The General Assembly decided to use this as a demonstration competition.

(9) The Philippine representative proposed that the tenth games be held in the third week of May 1934. The Chinese representative stated that they wish to hold them in August. This proposal will be considered later.

(10) The following officials were elected for the next games: Honorary President, Dr. Kishi Seiichi; President, Philippine Senate Speaker Quezon; First Vice President, Chinese Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting; Second Vice President, Philippine Fan Jiasi; Honorary Secretary, Philippine Yilanan.

Regulatory Commission

This Newspaper, May 31st, Tokyo: The Regulatory Commission discussed amateur sports rules and decided that sports instructors and gymnastics teachers should not be considered amateur athletes. The Philippine representative strongly opposed this. This matter will be discussed further by the subcommittee. The general public now believes that to improve the noble spirit of athletes, gymnastics teachers may not be considered amateur athletes by the public.

Yesterday a disturbance occurred in the Philippine-Japan boxing match

Referee Unfair, Philippines Withdraws from Final

Order in chaos, spectators want ticket refunds

This Newspaper, May 31st, Tokyo: Today's Japanese-Philippine open boxing final was well attended. After the lightweight competition, the Philippine athletes were unwilling to participate in the light and featherweight finals because of the unfair referee and other rematches. They were unwilling to compete again. The referee announced that the Philippine team had forfeited. The audience was in an uproar because there was no competition. They wanted ticket refunds and the order was in chaos. Afterwards, the Philippine coach Delonger announced three reasons: (1) The Philippines had notified the Japanese boxing registration that there must be strict restrictions because the final was scheduled on the closing day and the final time was uncertain. However, the Japanese committee ignored it. This not only hinders world boxing rules but also does not fit Philippine customs. Now they want us to have two games in one day. This is a lack of competition knowledge. (2) The final order was originally scheduled for 4:00 PM on the 31st, but it was suddenly advanced to 1:00 PM. This is detrimental to the Philippine team. (3) If the next games want to use boxing as a championship game, the treatment of guest teams must be improved. The unfair treatment of this game should be removed immediately. Otherwise, international sports exchanges will suffer significant losses, etc.

Closing and Awards Last Night

The Games Announces

First: Japan

Second: China

Third: Philippines

Fourth: India

May 31st, Tokyo: The Ninth Far Eastern Games were held at the Shinjuku Gyoen Chichibu Palace Reception after the completion of various competitions. The various committees and athletes attended. At 7:00 PM, the closing ceremony was held at the Japan Youth Association in Meiji Jingu Gaien. The flags of the four countries were hung in the auditorium. One hour before the meeting, the Games movies were shown to please the athletes. At 7:00 PM, Vice President Tanaka, Minister of Culture, President Kishi, and representatives of various countries entered the venue. The military band played Chinese and local tunes. His Majesty the Emperor's brother, Chichibu Palace, arrived. First, President Kishi delivered the closing speech, followed by brief speeches by Vice President Tanaka, Chinese Representative Zhang Boling, Philippine Representative Gongsi, and Indian Representative Mogaqi, etc. Then, prizes were awarded to the countries that won the championships in various sports. Then, the ranking of this year's games was announced: Japan first, China second, Philippines third, and India fourth. The crowd cheered and dispersed.

The volleyball silver shield made by this museum was won by the Chinese team. Wang Kai took the photo. The soccer silver shield made by this museum is temporarily kept by the Games. Wang Kai took the photo.

Men's Volleyball Championship

Chinese Volleyball Team Wins the Championship in a Thrilling Victory Over the Philippines

Winning Two Sets to One After Losing the First

First Set: 16 to 21

Second Set: 21 to 16

Third Set: 21 to 17

Mission Accomplished, Flag Raising Celebration

This newspaper's Tokyo dispatch, dated the 30th:

The Chinese and Philippine volleyball teams, long-time rivals, once again competed for the championship in this year's games with equal records of three wins and one loss each. The final deciding match was full of twists and turns and dramatic changes. In the end, the Chinese team, exerting tremendous effort, won two sets to one and seized the championship. It is noted that out of the eight championships in this year's games, except for soccer, which remains to be resolved in the next games, all others have fallen into the hands of other countries. The only remaining achievement for our country is this volleyball championship.

The Only Hope

All other championships have gone to others. According to reason, China should have no difficulty winning the soccer championship again. However, in order to realize their long-held ambition, the Japanese would rather go against established regulations and disregard public opinion to obstruct China's efforts. The championship that China had long maintained was thus snatched away unexpectedly. The only hope lies in the volleyball event.

Everyone Rejoices

The patriotic fervor of the overseas Chinese was fervent. They tirelessly ran to each venue every day to cheer and support the team from the sidelines. However, the results often left them sighing in disappointment. Now that the deciding match between China and the Philippines had arrived, the anticipation for the championship was high. People came together in groups, friends and companions alike, and the cheers could be heard everywhere. When the intense match concluded and victory was achieved, they danced and celebrated, and everyone rejoiced.

Watching Intently

When the referees Takahashi and Toyoshima arrived, the Chinese and Philippine athletes entered the arena one after another amidst the cheers of the crowd. They engaged in light exercises to loosen their muscles, sharpening their fists and preparing to fight. They were watching intently, as if they had an eternal feud to resolve once and for all.

Heartbroken

As the battle began, the Filipinos served powerfully and defended nimbly, adding clean passes and powerful spikes. The score quickly increased, and soon they took a 9-0 lead. At this point, the spectators were heartbroken, despairing of the future. China's initial disadvantage was due to being too eager to win, which led to excessive moves. Later, they made a concerted effort to catch up, and Cao Tingzan finally scored two points. However, the opposing team's front row was excellent, so they switched formations with a score of 11-2.

Three Heroes Emerge

Our team combined its efforts and defended skillfully, and the situation gradually turned around. Cao Tingzan, Xu Heng, and Qiu Guangxie emerged as powerful spikers, constantly launching fierce attacks and closing the gap. However, the opponent's first row was too good, so the effect was limited. Nevertheless, both sides used innovative methods to counter each other, putting on a wonderful performance that was praised by the crowd. Eventually, China and the Philippines reached a tie at 16 points each.

In One Breath

After the tie, the Filipinos were greatly shocked and changed their strategy, focusing their attacks on the third row. China's defensive line was slightly relaxed, and loopholes appeared repeatedly. The Philippines took advantage of this and, in one breath, won the first set with a score of 21-16.

The Bearing of Renowned Generals

The second set saw a different situation, with our team showing its might again. The bearing of renowned generals was indeed different. With smooth cooperation, they performed several amazing spikes. Zhu Zucheng's performance was particularly outstanding, and Qiu Guangxie's serves were also effective. China took an early lead of 4-0. The Filipinos tried several times and eventually tied the score at 5-5. Both sides defended and attacked skillfully, proving themselves worthy opponents. Cao Tingzan and Chen Xiyan maintained the pressure and soon switched sides with a score of 11-7.

A Sudden Turn

After that, both sides' warriors were filled with spirit, and the ball flew back and forth unpredictably. Our team took advantage of the momentum and struck fearlessly. Chen Xibing made several killer shots, and the situation suddenly turned around. In an instant, they won the second set with a score of 21-16, tying the overall score at one set each.

Danger Again

With the score tied at one set each, the championship would be decided in the final third set. The atmosphere was tense, and the situation was serious. In the fierce battle between the two sides, China initially took a 4-2 lead. Then, they repeatedly touched the net and failed to save the ball, allowing the Philippines to gain momentum and exchange sides with a score of 11-7.

Three Changes Turn the Tide

At this point, there were doubts about the only hope for the championship. It was hanging in the balance, and no one knew who would win it. Fortunately, Gui Rong replaced Xu Heng, and China gained a new force, greatly strengthening their strength. All the athletes did their best and worked hard, hoping to seize a glimmer of hope in this decisive moment. Sure enough, with a difference of 7-11, they first changed the score to 11-14, then to 15-17, and finally to a tie at 17.

Mission Accomplished

After the three changes, the atmosphere was full of vitality. The balls spiked by Qiu Guangxie, Cao Tingzan, and Chen Xibing were as fierce as tigers, and the Filipinos could not resist and felt it difficult to defend and attack. When China reached 20 points and the Philippines reached 17 points, the Philippines still fought like a cornered beast, hoping for a miracle. However, our army's momentum had been established, and reaching the goal of victory seemed as easy as turning over a hand. Soon, they won the third set with a score of 21-17, winning the volleyball championship with an overall score of two sets to one.

Flag Raising Celebration

Our country's only volleyball championship had been won as desired. The Chinese flag was raised high on the giant pillars in the games' venue, fluttering in the wind and creating a magnificent scene. The entire venue stood up to pay tribute, and people from various countries congratulated each other. The victorious athletes were surrounded and could hardly get away, truly a grand occasion.

The Bearing of a Hero

After the volleyball match between China and the Philippines, the reporter met with the Philippine coach, Ermonte, who said that his team's cohesion was no less than that of China's, but they could not score more points due to a lack of spiking power. Comparing the strength of the three countries, Japan was the weakest, and China and the Philippines seemed equal, but China had three killers whose hits were sure to score. He added that Li Lianying's swift and unusual left-handed spikes were beyond human ability. He said that the Philippine team should admit defeat this time because they had done their best in every way. According to reports, this statement by the Filipinos did not lack the bearing of a hero.

Men's Baseball Championship

Japan Wins Again Against the Philippines

Eight to Five

This newspaper's Tokyo dispatch, dated the 20th: Today, Japan won again against the Philippines with a score of eight to five. Details are as follows:

The Japanese baseball team, with its overwhelming momentum of winning every battle, defeated the Philippines again yesterday with a score of eight to five, winning the championship. The scores for each inning are as follows:

1 2 3 4 5 6 7 8 9 Score

Country　　　　Inning Inning Inning Inning Inning Inning Inning

Japan　　　　0 0 0 0 0 0 0 1 7 8

Philippines　0 0 1 0 0 0 1 3 0 5

The Philippines Displays Great Prowess

At the time, the performance of one of the winning teams did not seem appropriate for a championship team, giving the Philippines a great opportunity. They started off by scoring one point in the third inning, then another point in the seventh inning, and then added three more in the eighth inning, taking a 5-0 lead.

The Japanese Work Hard to Win the Championship

Despite being in an unfavorable situation, the Japanese continued to work hard, hoping to recover and maintain their reputation for winning every game. In the bottom half of the eighth inning, the Japanese woke up like a sleeping lion and displayed unstoppable might. The Philippine defense line was completely broken, and they immediately began to score one point. In the ninth inning, they launched a large-scale attack, and runners continuously returned to home base. They eventually took the lead, scoring a total of seven points. As a result, the Japanese won with a score of eight to five. Overall, although the Philippines lost, their performance was better. The Philippines and Japan each had nine hits, and Japan had three errors while the Philippines only had two.

Not only were there five athletes, but two referees were added, turning into seven people. In our hearts, we only see China as our strong opponent. The Japanese are not worth mentioning. China has the most perfect sportsmanship, which is worthy of our admiration and sympathy. China's defeat is due to its inability to have the courage that we have and to fight not only the enemy but also the referees.

Men's Basketball Championship

Philippines Beats Japan to Win the Championship

Forty-Five to Forty

This newspaper's Tokyo dispatch, dated the 30th:

The basketball finals between the Philippines and Japan drew great attention because Japan had defeated the Philippine Islands before and was expected to win again. When the match started at 7:30 PM on Friday night, the venue was packed with countless people. The referees were Tanaka and Fujimachi.

The Referee Secretly Helps the Japanese to Gain Momentum

At the beginning, the Japanese cooperated well and shot accurately, taking an 8-0 lead. The Philippines missed several opportunities in the first five minutes. However, the referee's decisions were chaotic and unfair, so the Philippines' opponent was not the warriors but the referee. Incidents happened repeatedly, almost causing the game to stop, and an unhappy atmosphere filled the venue. With this secret help, the Japanese won the first half with a score of 22-18.

Furious and Determined to Win the Championship

From the beginning of the second half, the referee became even more unreasonable, adding countless penalties. The Filipinos were furious and defended with all their might. Platt, Lasso, and Peromi fought like crazy. As expected, they turned the situation around and won the basketball championship with a score of 45-40.

The Filipinos Show Dissatisfaction Despite Winning

After the match, the Philippine team captain, Lasso, told reporters that the refereeing in this year's competition was the worst in history. Although we won, we are not satisfied. We respect our opponents Hua (center), Chen (right forward), Huang (center forward), Liang Zhaowen (left forward), and Chen Zhenxing.

In the second group of the 400-meter freestyle heat, Shi Xinglong from our country came in fourth with a time of six minutes and sixteen seconds, approximately sixty meters behind the first place. In the first group of the 200-meter breaststroke heat, Yang Yuanhua participated but failed to qualify.

This newspaper's Tokyo dispatch, dated the 31st:

On the morning of the 29th, the Hiroshima Girls' School Athletic Association held a welcome reception for the female athletes from various countries at the First Girls' High School in Tokyo. Approximately sixty Japanese athletes participated. The principal, Ichikawa, delivered a welcome speech, and representatives from China and the Philippines responded. Afterwards, there were entertainment programs such as singing and dancing. Finally, the Athletic Association presented souvenirs before the event ended.

Tokyo Cantonese Overseas Chinese Club At the same time, the Tokyo Cantonese Overseas Chinese Club also held a reception for our country's athletes at the Chinese YMCA. There were approximately two hundred guests. Several speeches were given, mostly encouraging the athletes to continue to work hard and prepare for the next games. However, someone lamented the unfairness of the refereeing in ball games and requested that the committee raise the necessary protests.

Far Eastern Women's Association In the afternoon, the Far Eastern Women's Association hosted a banquet for members from China and the Philippines at the Noble School.

Pacific Problems Research Association The Pacific Problems Research Association also hosted a banquet for Zhang Boling in the afternoon. Zhang spoke about how the Pacific problem is currently the most important issue in the world, and the Far East problem is particularly important in international affairs. To maintain world peace, the Pacific problem must be resolved peacefully.

Tokyo YMCA Last night, the Tokyo YMCA hosted a simple banquet for our country's athletes, with entertainment programs such as young girls playing the piano and young children playing the violin.

Review of the Four Nations' Contests (Dao Sheng)

The grand and spectacular 9th Far Eastern Games concluded last night. As a result, Japan won the overall championship, China came in second, the Philippines came in third, and India came in last.

The Reasons for China's Failure

The Chinese team's performance, which was eagerly anticipated by the people of the whole country, was mediocre and unexpected. Although they won the second place, their results were worse than in the last games, so they had to admit defeat. However, there are two main reasons for this: (1) Our country is good at ball games, especially soccer, volleyball, and basketball, which are the most promising. However, news came that selfishness and lack of cooperation led to failure. The complete defeat of the basketball team is proof of this. (2) Japanese referees are often influenced by their emotions and forget their independent position. This has been the case in every game, but it is especially true this time, causing an unhappy atmosphere in the perfect games. Once our country's progressive class is obstructed by them, even if they strive for fairness, they will eventually fail and have to declare defeat. The illegal handling of soccer by the Japanese is clear evidence of this. From this example, the rest can be imagined.

Japan's Shortcomings

Japan's excellent performance and victory were expected. However, due to excessive emphasis, they did not hesitate to abandon the attitude and means of being upright and just, causing the representatives from China and the Philippines to sigh and regret. It is a great pity.

The Philippines Almost Completely Lost

The Philippines' talent is average. Their goal is not the championship, but to compete with China for the second place. However, they failed and fell to third place. Fortunately, they seized the basketball championship from the Japanese, avoiding a complete defeat. This is also a great fortune in misfortune.

India Is Glorious Even in Defeat

The Indians went to Japan with great courage and resolutely participated, fulfilling their membership duties. They put the results of victory or defeat behind them. Their display of national spirit was enough to impress the countries, and their fight for the flag was full of integrity. Their glory will last for thousands of years.

Venue Anecdotes (Sent by Qu from Tokyo)

The Games Do Not Keep Time

The games were scheduled to open at noon on the 24th, but when the noon cannon sounded, the long hand of the clock had already passed five minutes. Aside from the clanging of the phonograph records on the stage, there was no sound. A Chinese lady in the audience said with a mocking tone, "The Japanese don't keep time either." It is understandable that the affairs of the games are numerous and difficult to arrange, and it is not necessary to criticize a delay of a few minutes. However, the Japanese are known for their strict adherence to schedules for trains, ships, etc. It is no wonder that they are subject to criticism for revealing this flaw at the opening ceremony of this grand and solemn games.

The Disobedient Phonograph

To alleviate the audience's boredom before the opening ceremony, phonograph records were played on the sound amplifier in front of the stage. When the distinguished guests were about to take their seats, the headquarters shouted loudly to stop the phonograph. However, the driver was flustered and only made the machine louder, causing laughter throughout the venue.

The Demeanor of Chinese Athletes

When the athletes entered the arena in formation, the Chinese team took the lead, with Lu Ming and Li Guochen holding the flag on either side, and the Chen sisters, who were very outstanding. When the athletes took the oath, Mr. Zhang Linjia represented our country. Mr. Zhang was tall and strong with a loud voice, complementing the tall and fat Dr. Zhang Boling on the stage. The representatives from other countries such as the Philippines, India, and Japan were either unattractive or had low voices, and they were not as impressive as our country's leader.

Baseball Victory Against the Philippines

At 2:30 PM on the afternoon of the first day of the games, the first baseball match between China and the Philippines was held. In the fourth inning, our army had already scored three points, while the Philippine army was still at zero. Their pitcher made many mistakes, causing the catcher to sweat profusely. He suddenly disliked his glove and took it off to adjust it, then took off his helmet, not knowing where to put it. He then clamped it between his legs. His anxious situation was quite amusing. In the seventh inning of the baseball game, Feng Yuhe and Zhang Rongan of our army stole bases twice, which was very agile. In the eighth inning, the Philippine army had a full base, but Zheng Fa, the pitcher of our army, managed to survive the crisis by throwing six strikes in a row, completely wiping out the enemy. In the end, our army won against the Philippines with a score of 9-6, earning applause from the whole venue.

India's Double National Flag

India was a new addition to this year's games, with only three athletes. Quantity was secondary to quality. These few athletes were very popular with the audience. The opening remarks and congratulatory messages were all the same, welcoming India's new participation. However, before the opening ceremony, there was a question about the national flag. Some people thought that India was a British colony and had not yet become independent, and they were worried about the British embassy in Japan. Therefore, the British flag should be used. Others thought that Gandhi was leading the Indian people in an anti-British movement, and Gandhi's white, green, and red fan-shaped flag was the true national flag of India. As a result, the British flag was still used. Indian revolutionaries who had fled to Japan issued a statement denying that the three athletes represented India. Today (the 24th), the Indian team took a compromise approach, carrying both the British flag and Gandhi's flag, creating the strange sight of a double national flag.

The Municipal Education Bureau Promulgates the Graduation Examination Methods for Municipal Secondary Schools

The Senior High School Education Bureau Sends Personnel to Supervise the Preliminary Secondary School Entrance Examination

The Shanghai Special Municipal Education Bureau issued an order to all secondary schools yesterday, stating that in order to comply with the regulations on the management of student graduation examinations in secondary schools, the graduation examinations of secondary schools must be reported in advance for supervision. In order to be serious, the Bureau has formulated a detailed method. All senior high schools handling graduation shall comply with Articles 1, 2, and 3 of the Regulations on the Management of Student Graduation in Primary and Secondary Schools, report the examination methods and procedures in advance, and fill in and submit the forms. During the examination, the Bureau will send personnel to the school to supervise the examination. All junior high schools handling graduation shall decide to hold a joint examination. All junior high schools shall immediately fill in and submit a list of students in the graduating class to the Bureau and notify the graduating students to prepare a four-and-a-half-inch half-length photo to be submitted during the first joint examination. The joint examination method has been formulated and a copy is enclosed for compliance. This order is issued for compliance.

Junior Middle School Graduation Examination Regulations

(A) Examination Subjects: (1) Party Principles (2) Chinese Language (3) English Language (4) (Chinese and Foreign) History (5) Chinese and Foreign Geography (6) Mathematics (7) Natural Sciences (B) Percentages of Importance of Each Subject are as Follows: (1) Party Principles (2) Chinese Language Twenty-Seven (3) English Language Eighteen (4) History Nine (5) Geography Nine (6) Mathematics Twenty-Two (7) Natural Sciences Eleven (C) Examination of Grades (1) Grade Levels for Each Subject are Divided into Five Levels: A, B, C, D, and E. The Index Values Assigned to Each Level are as Follows: A｜4 B｜3 C｜2 D｜1 E｜0 (2) Method of Scoring Grades: For Example, if Zhang Sheng's Grades in Each Subject are: Party Principles: Grade A, then 4 x 4 = 16; Chinese Language: Grade B, then 27 x 3 = 81; English Language: Grade C, then 18 x 2 = 36; History: Grade D, then 9 x 1 = 9; Geography: Grade E, then 9 x 0 = 0; Mathematics: Grade A, then 22 x 4 = 88; Natural Sciences: Grade B, then 11 x 3 = 33. Therefore, Zhang Sheng's Total Score is 263, and 263 x 100 = 263. All scores at 0 or above will be counted as one grade higher. So Zhang Sheng's overall grade for junior high school graduation is B. (D) Graduation Standards: (1) Students with overall grades of A or B in all subjects are eligible to graduate. (2) Students with overall grades of D in any subject must take a make-up exam for part or all of the subjects. They can only graduate after the assessed grades are passing. (3) Students with overall grades of E in any subject cannot graduate and must retake part or all of the subjects. (E) Examination Dates: June 16th, Monday, 8:30 AM to 11:30 AM, Party Principles; 1:30 PM to 4:30 PM, Chinese Language. June 17th, Tuesday, 8:30 AM to 11:30 AM, English Language; 1:30 PM to 4:30 PM, History. June 18th, Wednesday, 8:30 AM to 11:30 AM, Geography; 1:30 PM to 4:30 PM, Mathematics. June 19th, Thursday, 8:30 AM to 11:30 AM, Natural Sciences. (F) Examination Locations for Each School: (1) The Guangzhao Middle School in Chongde Lane, North Sichuan Road, north of the Yokohama Bridge, will host the examinations for: Municipal Wusong Junior High School, Private Nanfang Middle School, Private Guangzhao Middle School, Private Yanmoushi Girls' School, Private Zhonghua Middle School, Private Guangdong Middle School, Private Huai'en Middle School, Private Fudan Experimental Middle School, Private Lida Middle School, Private Xinmin Middle School, Private Minsheng Middle School, Private Danhua Middle School, Private Daozhong Girls' Middle School, Private Chongde Girls' Middle School, Private Qixiu Middle School, Private Chizhi University Affiliated Middle School, Private Nanyang Advanced Business Middle School, Private Aiguo Girls' Middle School, Private Shibei Middle School, Private Jianguo Middle School, Private Mingqiang Middle School. (2) The Private Minli Middle School on Zhonghua Road will host the examinations for: Municipal Wuben Girls' Middle School, Municipal Jingye Middle School, Private Minli Middle School, Private Minli Girls' Middle School, Private Bowen Girls' Middle School, Private Huiling Middle School, Private Baiwen Girls' Middle School, Private Chengdong Girls' Middle School, Private Aiqun Girls' Middle School, Private Qingxin Middle School, Private Qingxin Girls' Middle School, Private Shenmei Girls' Middle School, Private Junyi Middle School, Private Yucai Middle School. (3) The Private Datong University on Jiaozhou Road will host the examinations for: Private Huzhou Shanghai Middle School, Private Sanyu Middle School, Private Minzhi Middle School, Private Qingnian Middle School, Private Wuxing Middle School, Private Shangxian Middle School, Private Zhongxi Girls' School, Private Qinghua Middle School, Private Fudan University Affiliated Middle School, Private Shanghai Girls' School, Private Nanyang Model Middle School, Private Qingnian Middle School, Private Guanghua University Affiliated Middle School, Private Mailun Middle School, Private Dongwu Second Middle School, Private Jinglin Middle School, Private Zhaoshang Middle School, Private Huiqun Girls' Middle School, Private Chengzhong Middle School, Private Daxia Middle School, Private Zhirenyong Girls' Middle School, Private Peiming Girls' Middle School, Private Yalu Middle School, Private Zhende Girls' Middle School, Private Zhengfeng Middle School, Private St. Mary's Girls' School, Private Peicheng Girls' Middle School, Private Huahua Middle School, Private Hujiang University Affiliated Middle School. (4) Private Pudong Middle School will hold the examinations at its original location. (G) Important Announcements: (1) All municipal and private junior high schools or junior high school departments should gather at the designated addresses on time for the examination. (2) During the examination, students should only bring pens and ink boxes and are not allowed to bring books or other items. They should also abide by the examination rules. (3) Any middle school that has been approved for registration but does not comply will have its registration revoked. (5) Any middle school that has not been registered but does not comply will be strictly banned. (6) Junior high school students who have not been registered, but pass the examination, will have the words "Graduation Grade Assessed and Passed by the Shanghai Special City Education Bureau" added to their graduation certificates, which will allow them to apply to public or approved private schools at all levels. (7) Municipal, approved or unapproved middle schools whose students' graduation results are indeed excellent will be publicly rewarded separately. (8) Lunch during the examination will be provided by this bureau, and the cost of the meals must be reimbursed by the respective schools. (9) Transportation for students to and from the examination will be arranged by each school. (10) After the examination grades have been assessed, the names of all junior high school graduates in the city will be disclosed in the newspapers. (11) Each student must prepare a half-length four-inch photograph to be submitted when taking the Party Principles exam on the 16th.
