Free Talk

One Word of Wisdom by Qiushui

Love is the stimulant of the heart, the anesthetic of the brain, and the hypnotic pill of common sense.

Lying is a fault in children, an art in suitors, a success in the unmarried, but the second nature of married men and women.

In principle, men are never willing to tell women the truth, even though they know that not lying is more beneficial to them.

Almost every man can make a woman believe that black is white, but to make her think that black is the red of a rose, one must have the artistic skill.

In business or in gambling, a man has strong self-control and precise planning, but on the battlefield of love, every man is like a car coming down from a high mountain, difficult to control.

To make a woman love you, there is a technique: focus your eyesight, your heart, and your spirit on one woman at the same time.

Young women like men to be dazzled when they see them, while old women like men to be encouraged when they see them.

Many men have an empty heart to love two women, but few have the brains to love two women at the same time.

Many lovers and married men and women never realize the joy of being together until they feel lonely after they leave each other.

Many men and women marry for convenience, not for love. Men and women who marry purely for love will never divorce.

Anecdotes About Cheng Xuelou by Shiyu

The first governor of my Jiangsu was Cheng Gong Xuelou. In September of the Xinhai year, Cheng Gong, following public opinion, made a sweeping reform. He remained unmoved by the seven chaos. What great merit and virtue he had for my Jiangsu! It is said that if a certain official had been the governor at that time, he would have stubbornly resisted with his own ideas, and the disaster would have been unimaginable. Now I hear that Cheng Gong has returned to the mountains, which makes people feel sad. His achievements are like his. He resigned in the second year of the Republic of China and entered the monastery. The divine dragon sees the head but not the tail. His worldly old eyes can be said to be flowerless. Someone recounted an anecdote about him, saying that Cheng Gong started his career as a county magistrate, actually appointed to a county in the three eastern provinces. At that time, he had a thorny negotiation with a certain country. The country wantonly made demands and then used intimidating means, dragging artillery to show that it would bombard the people. However, Cheng Gong did not retreat, stepped forward, and stood with his abdomen covering the muzzle of the cannon, saying, "Just bombard Cheng, it has nothing to do with the people." The people of the country were surprised and respected him, and the negotiation gave way a lot, so it was fine. The next year, the Empress Dowager enjoyed the wives of foreign ministers. During the conversation, she sighed that our country's officials were mostly afraid and unable to do their best for the people. The wife of a certain minister said, "There is now a county magistrate in a certain county in the three eastern provinces who can give up his life, not be afraid of death, and plead for the people." Because of the above, the Empress Dowager told the eunuch to find out the truth and know that it was Cheng Dequan, so she wrote down his name and promoted him out of order. After a few years, he opened his government in my Wu. Wu got this virtuous head of state as a guarantee. How lucky he was! It is a pity that he resigned so quickly. Now that the eminent monk has passed away, he has received and returned completely. The public has no regrets. Can our people not feel more grateful because of the rapid changes in the world?

A Visit to the Slaughterhouse by Cheng Zhizheng

On the 26th of this month, the students of the Municipal Administration Class of the third grade of Jiaotong University in this city, led by Professor Tang, visited the slaughterhouse in Hongkou. What I heard and saw is worth mentioning, so I will list it to fill this talk.

The smell of blood assaulted the nose. At about two o'clock, as I entered, the smell of blood made people want to vomit. At the same time, blood accumulated on the cement floor, forming a canal. All the meat supply in Shanghai mostly depends on this place. The workers came and went, looking quite anxious. My companions and I all covered our noses and passed by.

The Westerner received us. Soon, a Westerner came out to receive us, quite amiable and approachable. He explained various situations to us in detail, saying that this place slaughters more than 50 cattle, more than 100 pigs, and dozens of sheep every day. All kinds of meat are tested one by one. Those that are complete and flawless are classified as first-class, and those that are slightly emaciated or slightly diseased are classified as second-class. Those that are diseased are discarded. All the prepared meat products are sold in the market immediately after slaughter.

The Westerner led us to explain each part of the work in detail. First, we went to the leather department, where the workers scraped the meat off the skin of the cattle and then folded the skin into a rectangle and sold it to the leather factory for about 27 cents per pound. Then we entered a huge room with many slaughtered cattle hanging inside. Each one was stamped. Walking among them was like entering a forest of meat. The pigs and sheep were also prepared in the same way. After dissecting the abdomen, air was pumped into the skin to make the meat swell, and the work was completed.

Procedures for Slaughtering Cattle: When slaughtering cattle, the cattle's brain is first struck with an iron hammer to stun the cattle before slaughtering them, which also reduces their pain. However, a workroom contains various handguns, which are used to shoot the heads of cattle. In England, this procedure for slaughtering livestock is stipulated by law. Now, to avoid trouble, the method of shooting with bullets has been changed to striking with a hammer. However, the cattle suffer. After the cattle are killed, they are dismembered. The various tasks are completed in a short time. Because machines are not used, the efficiency is certainly not comparable to that of the Chicago slaughterhouse. (Note: I have already recorded the Chicago slaughterhouse in this publication.)

Cattle Poisoning Test: Meat food places the highest importance on hygiene, so poisoning testing is the most important task. The Westerner showed us the lungs of a cow with lung disease. The spots were numerous, which was frightening. If people eat it, it is unimaginable. Later, we went to visit the cattle farm, about dozens of steps away. There were many cattle stored, all prepared for execution the next day. It is said that the cattle and sheep mostly come from the Danyang and Changzhou areas. The price of each head varies, from tens of yuan to hundreds of yuan. However, they are mostly thin and pitiful. Mencius said, "Hearing its voice, one cannot bear to eat its flesh," and "I cannot bear to see its trembling." Although we came here for academic research, I am afraid that when we recall this scene in the future, we will inevitably throw down our chopsticks and stop eating. The Westerner also said that to test whether a cow is poisonous, you can first hold its horn. If it is not sick, the horn must be cool, otherwise, it must be hot. Also, the ears of normal cattle must stand upright. The ears of sick cattle often hang down, and even the hair is related. This kind of common sense identification does not require dissection to know.

Rest for a Day: Livestock transported to Shanghai on the same day are temporarily kept and fed in this farm because they are tired from the boat and car. It is not suitable to slaughter them until the next day. Also, the day before slaughter, they cannot be fed feed and must be allowed to go hungry before being executed. This is also a way of hygiene, but it is far from the heart of benevolence.

Dog Prison: In addition to the cattle farm, there is also a dog prison, mostly for foreign hunting dogs. When asked why they are here, they said, "These are dogs that have bitten people." They are detained here for ten days to test whether they have mental illness. If not, they will be released after a ten-day sentence. This thorough management cannot but impress people. At about four o'clock, we said goodbye to the instructor and dispersed.

Talking About the Cuckoo by Qing

The cuckoo is a migratory bird. Every spring and early summer, its voice sounds like calling "(cut wheat and plant rice)," but the old farmers in my hometown harmonize its sound into a change like "(every family grows flowers)." Because rice seedlings are not transplanted at this time, cotton seeds must also be planted, so this bird is also called "(tillage bird)," which has a profound meaning. However, there is no Duke Ye Chang in the world, so no one can translate the language of this bird.

According to Erya, it is also called "(Shijiu)" and "(Hug)," saying that it is the cuckoo. Other books such as Yue Ling say "(Bo Gu)," Ben Cao says "(Bo Gu)," Fang Yan says "(Ji Gu)," and some books say "(Bu Gu)," or think that they are all transliterations of cuckoo. Their saying is not true, and Jiangyi East calls it "(Huo Gu)." Guo commented that it is a dove that calls for rain, then it is mistaken for "(Bu Gu)" and regarded as the same kind as the turtledove. I don't know that its voice is very different. In the past, Yu of Deqing pointed out that the dove cannot make a nest and did not refer to it as a turtledove, but regarded the turtledove as it. Zhang Taiyan also regarded the cuckoo as a turtledove, and their loss was the same. I recited Fang Weng's poem "Early Summer" and said first (The red and purple flowers have become dust in succession, and the summer season is new in the sound of the cuckoo). Then I felt that the sound of this bird was noisy, and between the fields, the yellow clouds of wheat ridges turned into a vast expanse of blue-green in an instant, and the rice seedlings were like hair needles. Its bird shape is like "(cuckoo)," but its body is larger, its color is gray-black, and its jaw is slightly white with line patterns across its chest and abdomen. Its flight is very slow and it sometimes makes a call. The difference is that it often lives alone without a partner. After this spring plowing and summer weeding, it disappears. Some call it "(divine bird)," which is hard to believe. My friend Li Jun Shijing said that a certain Western naturalist once studied that this bird can lay eggs but cannot incubate them. When it sees eggs that have already been laid in the nests of other birds, it often takes the opportunity to also lay eggs among them, fearing that the other birds will become suspicious because of the increase in the number of eggs. It must use its claws to pick out its original eggs to cover up its tracks. When its chicks come out, the other birds know that they are not of their own kind and are unwilling to feed them. Therefore, this bird, even as a young bird, is cunning among the chicks and can exert its fat and tender wings to lift the other chicks out of their nests and push them down. Then it can eat its fill to grow up. Once its feathers are full, it flies away and lives alone. He also said that he had taken a video of the bird's bizarre transformations, which cannot be imitated by other birds. Seeing this is also enough to provide for scholars' research. It is a pity that its source cannot be clearly indicated, which is still regrettable. I therefore narrate it, and I hope that the biologists in the world will also tell me about it.

The Female Knight-Errant of the Wasteland River on the Silver Screen by Bibo

My writing skills are dull and I cannot rely on words to survive. Instead, I go to the market to beg for food and haggle over every penny. From morning to night, I am so noisy that people regard me as an old peddler. After retiring, I often laugh at myself when I think about it. However, compared to my friend Gu Mingdao, whose physical constitution is weak, we are actually comparable. However, he is able to write thousands of words and wait for the horse to be saddled. In the most recent year, he has completed more than ten long articles such as Female Knight-Errant of the Wasteland River, Fragrant Grass at the End of the World, Record of the Crying of the Mandarin Duck, and Continued Record of the Cuckoo. This is enough to make us admire his speed of production. Female Knight-Errant of the Wasteland River was first published in newspapers, and millions of people recited it every day. Therefore, it is even more famous in the world. Once it was printed into a book,

It has already been published in three editions in a few months, and its popularity is evident. Because of this, the friend Lian Yin adopted this book to compile a film drama that is both positive and appropriate. The preparation and production took half a year and it was divided into four episodes: Havoc in Baolin Temple, Burning of the Han Family Village, Breaking the Beautiful Woman's Tower, and Double Investigation of White Bull Mountain. In each episode, there are clues that echo each other, woven with scenes of fragrant romance. The film emphasizes martial arts, but it must also take into account both expressive art. Ms. Xu Qinfang plays the protagonist. Her beauty and liveliness make her a pleasant and enjoyable role. For the sake of solemnity, Chen Kangran, Zheng Yisheng, and Shang Guanwu jointly directed the film, and the shooting method is particularly novel and unparalleled. The first and second episodes of the film have been scheduled to be shown for six consecutive days at the Central Grand Theater starting on the 30th of this month, and a stage play will also be performed, in which the characters in the play will perform on stage with melodious and circuitous lyrics, sword light and sword shadow martial arts, mysterious and unpredictable scenery, and scenes of joy and sorrow. I would like to tell you that since you have a film with a majestic dragon-like aura, you will also have a grand opera with a magnificent dragon and tiger leaping performance. How wonderful is it to have such a feast for your ears and eyes?

Zhangshan Cloud Mist Tea by Diehua

Wuyuan is famous in the world for its tea production. Zhangshan green tea is the best quality among Wuyuan tea. Although its taste is superior, Longjing is inferior to it. At the top of Zhangshan Mountain, Bagua Peak, there are several wild tea trees growing horizontally on dangerous cliffs. The mountain people call it Cloud Mist Tea because the peak is often shrouded in clouds and mist, just like Mount Lu, which cannot be seen in its true form. The tea leaves are white in color, soft in texture, and pointed and long in shape. The taste is clear, sweet, and has a strange fragrance that is different from other teas. The mountain people pick it when the fog is transparent, using a long rope to tie a bamboo chair. The picker wraps the rope around his body and ties it in the chair. Several other people hold the long rope from the top of the cliff and slowly lower it to the tea. After picking, they pull it up. Although the method is simple, it is quite laborious. The mountain people hide this tea deeply and do not give it to people easily. It is not easy to buy with money. It is said that this tea is effective for treating heart and stomach problems and other diseases.

Warmth in the Heart (204) by Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Eleven: Emerald Hairpins and Pearl Hair Ornaments, Beautiful Women Return to Good Scholars; Green House and Red Tent, Famous Prostitutes Marry Famous Families

That Zhu Feng saw me whispering in Ruiyun's ear, and as soon as Ruiyun left, she said, "Second Young Master, are you asking her? You must not say that I told you. They will complain about me. According to the rules, sisters cannot talk nonsense about who is getting married and who is not in front of guests. I said, "Don't worry, I will definitely not say that you reported it. Besides, what you reported is not necessarily true. I have already explored her tone." After I finished eating, I came to the room next door. At that time, Ruiyun's performance was also over and she was changing clothes. I wanted to ask her what was going on, but people kept coming in and out of the room, and there was no chance to talk to her alone. Later, Ruiyun shouted that she was hungry and wanted to ask them to buy some snacks. I said, "I didn't eat enough just now either. Let's go to Yipinxing to eat big dishes. After eating the big dishes, I will go back." Ruiyun said yes without hesitation and called Ah Jin to accompany me. She also hurriedly went to change clothes. The big aunt was not in charge of business, so no one could stop her. Besides, with Ah Jin accompanying her, it would not violate their rules. Originally, Ah Jin was very helpful to Ruiyun. Wasn't there a disturbance about the Hou Party in the Guangxu Dynasty a few years ago? Ruiyun's room was like a small Qing Dynasty court. Only Ah Jin was like Weng Tonghe, Master Weng. The rest of the people in the room were all Ronglu and Yuan Shikai. Moreover, Master Weng was from Changshu, and Ah Jin was also from Changshu, which made them even more similar. We then took Master Weng to Yipinxing. No matter what we said, Ah Jin would never spread rumors. Ruiyun was indeed a little hungry. I went specifically to inquire about news. I intended to ask Ruiyun after she finished eating the big dishes, but just as she was eating soup, Ruiyun said to Ah Jin, "Just now, Second Young Master said that people outside are talking about someone named Zhao and someone named Wu." Ah Jin casually said, "Really?" I took the opportunity to ask, "Who is it, Zhao or Wu? Didn't you promise to tell me?" Ruiyun put the spoon in the soup dish and said, "I don't even know myself. Now my body is like in an auction house. Whoever bids the most will take it away." Later, according to the mutual accounts of Ruiyun and Ah Jin, there were originally three guests who wanted to marry Ruiyun at the same time: one was Zhao Qi, one was Wu San, and one was Zhuang Da. Zhao Qi was the youngest, only in his twenties. Wu San was a little older than Zhao Qi and had not reached forty years old. Only Zhuang Da was already in his forties this year. However, Zhao Qi was only willing to pay three thousand yuan because the economic power was still in the hands of his father. Three thousand yuan was still勉力available for籌措. Wu San was willing to pay four thousand yuan, but Wu San said that he was a little bit picky and not straightforward. The big aunt meant that she wanted five thousand yuan. However, although Zhuang Da also bargained for four thousand yuan, it seemed that he could manage to raise the full five thousand yuan because he was a famous wealthy man in Shanghai.

Silver Split in May Was Higher Than in Previous Months

Due to the overall weakness in silver supply in the past four months of this year, silver splitting has been difficult to turn upwards, so the monthly total is less than the statutory two liang. Only in the previous month, due to the occasional infighting among colleagues in the financial industry, did they compete with each other to hold interest rates, resulting in a rise of one or two cents. As a result, the total for the whole month was 4 liang and 0.05 points. Calculated on a thirty-day basis, the daily average is 1 cent, 3 mils and 5 micromils. Because last month had thirty-one days, if calculated on a thirty-one day basis, it would only account for 1 cent, 3 mils and 0.645 points per day. As such, the proposed opening interest rate benchmark for this month is probably around 4 liang and 95% off. Let's record this to see if it works.

The Time for Opening the Silver Split is Earlier

Set to Open at Eight O'Clock

Art World

Modern Danish Literature (Continued)

Zhao Jingshen's Lecture at Fudan University

Chen Xiemeng

Tang Zengyang's Notes

Among those who are not of the (Jutland School) type, the first we must mention is Nexo.

Nexo (Martin Andersen Nexo, 1864) his appearance represents another aspect of Danish thought, because his ideas are completely incompatible with those of the (Jutland School). He was born in Copenhagen, living in extreme poverty. At the age of nine, he moved with his parents to the island of Bornholm, the island where his father was born. After Nexo was confirmed, he worked as a shepherd and as a shoemaker's apprentice, but because he disliked being cooped up indoors, he later worked as a bricklayer's assistant and transporting bricks and tiles. Later, he entered Askov Folk High School. He loved to read and gained some knowledge, then began to write. At this time, he was nearly thirty years old. In 1898, he wrote a collection of short stories, *Shadows*, depicting the customs and conditions of Italy and Spain. In 1901, he wrote *The Frank Family*. In 1902, he wrote *Dry Rain*, which depicts darkness and pessimism using the techniques of naturalism, but these are not his representative works. His masterpiece is *Pelle the Conqueror* (I-IV, 1906-1910). The entire book consists of four volumes. The first volume depicts his childhood memories living in a stone house on Bornholm Island. The second volume depicts his work as an apprentice. The third volume depicts the spirit of resistance. The author created a protagonist who, according to the author himself, not only faithfully and kindly extols the traditional virtues of the poor but also portrays their ability to preserve the meaning of humorous conversation and happiness, as well as the beauty of life. The author gained international fame for *Pelle the Conqueror* and was able to lead workers towards the path of enlightenment. Nexo also has another important work, *Ditte, Daughter of Man*. In this book, the author writes about Ditte's story of being a female Pelle, which is even darker than Pelle's story. She is a pitiful maidservant whose life of hardship from cradle to grave is concentrated in her, causing endless pity.

Kund Hjorto (1869) writes novels that mostly depict rural squires. He was also a farmer's son. His first novel was *Neighbors*, published in 1901. Since then, he has published *Rasmus* (1909) and *Inside and Outside the Parish* (1919). His writings mostly involve social and psychological ideas with penetrating observation. He writes dialogue most realistically for women and children, but his books are difficult to read. In 1904 he wrote *Ashes and Stars*, in 1905 he wrote *Two Worlds*, and in 1906 he wrote *Hawo Daoko*. This trilogy is full of fantasy and passion. In 1921, he wrote *Faust*, a book containing many philosophical elements and questions about life and death. The author's novels are mostly short stories and have very few editions. For example, in China, each edition of a published book typically has around 2,000 copies, but his novels only have 500 to 800 copies per edition. Because they do not attract people's attention, the author is not easily famous in his own country, but he is very famous abroad.

Atto Rnuny (1874) wrote *The White Cruiser* in 1906, *Shadows of the Past* in 1909, *The Great Caravan* in 1914, *The Secret Chamber* in 1919, *The Isle of Bliss* in 1919, and *When the Water Settles* in 1922. He has many works and skillfully uses suspense, which is strong and surprising. The key to the author's novels is a tight interweaving, a kind of popular appeal that provides entertainment for the general public. For example, *The White Cruiser* and *The Great Caravan* can easily arouse a kind of stimulation in readers. There are many places in the book that show action, which is very noisy, like China's *Shi Gong An* and *Water Margin*. His novels, of course, belong to the old side: the old being noisy, and the new being silent and profound in people's views.

Harald Kidde (1878-1918) his descriptions penetrate to the depths, able to fully understand people with different thoughts and are very sympathetic to those who suffer. His writing style is solemn and contemplative, and he has many works. (1) *Allegorical Paintings* (1900) is a collection of allegories. (2) *Aage and Else* (1902-1903) is a long Danish nursery rhyme story. The book writes about a dead warrior who is resurrected because of his lover's grief, but soon dies again, revealing the victory of death over life. The protagonist, Tne Tavsen, is a melancholic patient who sees many lovers die for him and wants to revive lull wedev to make him live, but fails. The tragedy ends from this point forward. (3) *Castles in the Air* (1904). (4) *The Blind Man* (1906). (5) *The Law* (1909). (6) *Others* (1909). (7) *The Blessed* (1910). ((6) and (7) are optimistic). (8) *Heroes* (1912). (9) *Hunger* (1918). He abandoned theology in his early years but loved religious life and worked as a pitiful and contemptible teacher. Later, on a remote island, he proclaimed the light of God and the welfare of the people, abandoning his own dreams of happiness. *Hunger* depicts events in Sweden. The ideas in the book are difficult to unravel. The author died of the plague a few weeks after the book was published, at only forty-one years old.

Aage van Koht (1877) writes novels of savage decadence, including *Palace of Lichens* (I-III, 1908), which depicts the sinking of a warship and is full of terror and despair.

There are not as many female Danish writers as there are Swedish writers, and they are not as important, but there are also a few who are very famous.

Gyrith Semche (1866) is famous for her historical novels. Her most famous work is *Edwardsgaue* (I-IV, 1900-1912). Karin Michaelis (1872) her most famous works are psychological novels, including *The Broken Glass* (1924).

Thit Jensen (1876) spent some time in her youth living as a farmer. Her thoughts are very pure and full of passion. She feels that a fallen life is not worthy of being human. Later, she wrote a play, *The Stork*. It is a bird name in Nordic countries, according to legend, that this bird often brings babies to mothers. The play promotes birth control (To be continued).

Manuscript Guidelines for the Art World

(1) Articles should be limited to news, reviews, and introductions of recent art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature, both domestic and foreign.

(2) Pictures should be limited to recent works by new writers, both domestic and foreign, and accompanying illustrations related to the text.

(3) Photographs should be limited to recent portraits and works by domestic and foreign writers, and various photographs related to the text.

(4) Each article should not exceed 3,000 words.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, and do not write carelessly. Western text should be omitted whenever possible. If it is unavoidable to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink for illustrations in the manuscript, and do not use colored paper. White paper and black ink must be used.

Youth Corner

(Uncle Wen) Soniya in *Uncle Vanya*

Among the foreign literary writers I know, Chekhov of Russia is one of my favorites.

I haven't read many of his short stories, but every time I read one, it always leaves me with a very deep impression. His plays are much fewer in quantity than his novels, and I've read even fewer of them, but these few alone are enough to make me reluctant to put them down. His plays are written with the same skill and pen as his novels, so in them, as in his novels, you can't expect to find any legendary heroes, outstanding geniuses, or peerless beauties. What you see are just ordinary characters, characters that you can often find among your family members, among your friends, and around you if you pay a little attention. The content is just fragmented pieces of ordinary life's trivialities, reflecting the confusion and sadness of Russia at the end of the 19th century.

Works of this kind of subject matter move more or less readers of that time and modern readers. Once I heard the news that the works of my beloved playwright were being staged, it was truly something that made me ecstatic. Despite the inconvenience of transportation during the streetcar and bus strikes, it was absolutely unbearable for me not to go see the Xinyou Theatre Troupe's *Uncle Vanya*.

I don't want to criticize their performance this time now. Fortunately, the audience who has watched their previous performances, especially last year's *Dog's Dance*, has a public opinion. I just want to write down the unspeakable melancholy I felt when I walked home under the cold moonlight, which was not quite full, and on that desolate and mysterious street after watching the play that day. This melancholy was what I expected to receive before watching the play.

In *Uncle Vanya*, except for the two insignificant workers, everyone is living (miserable and tragic lives, pitiful and heartbroken people). Helen, Vanya, and Serebryakov go without saying, but even that professor who was envied by Vanya for saying (his romantic luck is so good, even the imperial bliss enjoyed by Emperor Tang in the past was no more than that), does he not have his sorrow?

Yes, everyone is a pitiful and heartbroken person, but I don't know why I would feel deep sympathy for Soniya (because of her ordinary appearance, no one loves). No, I actually fell in love with her.

Her life, her experiences, everything about her seemed somewhat familiar to me. She plucked at the strings of my heart, she stirred up my sorrow.

Yes, she is not just a hardworking and virtuous country girl, she has her own greatness. She cannot get used to (this desolate and lonely time, not meeting a decent person, only seeing this group of listless and lifeless things drifting around and saying boring things, knowing nothing but eating, drinking, and sleeping, bottom ghosts). She naturally wants to be happy like (seeing the moon come up in the dark night) to love that young doctor Zhao (so outstanding, so beautiful, so interesting, so lovely). Look how much she loves him. In the first act, in front of Dr. Zhao, she praised his enthusiasm and contributions to the forest, saying again and again that he said how the forest... (He said the forest would...). It flowed like reciting a running account. This can be imagined as a pitiful little girl reciting her lover's daily words in front of her bed every night before going to bed, word for word, once, twice, countless times, to replace her evening prayers.

In the second act, when she advises Dr. Zhao not to drink anymore, she is truly suffering. She truly loves him, she does not want him to (learn the behavior of those inferior people who drink and gamble), she does not want him to (destroy himself), but she is afraid of being presumptuous to say such immeasurable words in front of him. The pain of unrequited love.

She hesitantly and vaguely pretends to say that a friend or sister loves him to inquire about his tone, but the result is (there is no interest at all, his heart, his soul is still estranged from me, but how do I feel a bit of inexplicable happiness? I can't figure out what this is.)

This is a contradiction, but this is life.

If you fall in love with someone, you like to be with him or her, just like Soniya said to Dr. Zhao (It's rare for you to spend the night here.) (When you've finished seeing the patients, make sure to come back here for lunch.) (When will you come again... don't take a month, okay?). But when you are really together, you see that the other person (has no interest at all) in you, you will feel bored, you will feel sad, and at the same time, you will feel interested, like Soniya, savoring every move of Dr. Zhao, as if (I can still feel his voice vibrating in the air now.) (As if I hear him next to me all the time, I still feel his hand holding my hand tightly.) This is a contradiction, this cannot be explained by reason.

She loves him so passionately. In the third act, she said to her stepmother (I have loved him for six years, I love him more than I love my mother, but he never looks at me, the person in my eyes is not in his eyes.) She also said (I can't respect myself anymore, my heart is uncertain, I have no idea.)

Her stepmother promised to help her ask him to find out a little bit of his tone. She said (We just need to know if he has feelings or not, if not, then he must not come here in the future.)

The result is that she knows from her stepmother's mouth that he really (has no interest at all). She is deeply sinking into the abyss of despair.

But look, how does she solve her troubles?

In the fourth act, when she persuades her uncle to take out morphine, she says (My life is probably more bitter than yours, but I don't let go, I endure my pain and will continue to endure it as long as I have a breath left here.) She also said (Let's do something.)

(Let's do something, let's do something.) This is the author Chekhov using Soniya's mouth to say his own doctrine, using (work) to forget (distress). To me, this is a great revelation about life.

Perhaps some people say that the author is pessimistic and negates life, but at least in this play *Uncle Vanya*, he is optimistic and affirms life. Listen to Soniya's words (What can we do? We have to live our lives. We have to live those long days and long nights that follow. We have to patiently endure the tribulations destined for us. We have to take advantage of the present, just like we will when we are old, to work tirelessly for others. When our time comes

Page 28

We must die quietly, and when we get there, up there in heaven, we will declare the suffering and torment we have endured... then God will have mercy on us. Ah, we must see that bright and radiant life, we will rejoice and feel that now our troubles will fade away with a smile, and then we will rest... We will hear the voices of the angels, we will see the paradise as radiant as jewels, we will see all sins and all our pains melt into the great love that permeates heaven and earth. Our life will be as calm as an ancient well, as gentle as spring, and as sweet as honey. I believe... my poor Uncle Vanya, you have never tasted what happiness is, but wait, we will rest...)

In this world, perhaps there are people who are as distressed and pitiful as Soniya. I hope they will take a look at the great *Uncle Vanya*, which can give them some comfort and help them get rid of some distress.

Daxia Affiliated Public Night School

Holds Mandarin Speech Contest

The most number of out-of-school workers are in a corner of Western Shanghai. The school, in view of this, has achieved great success since its establishment. This spring, under the charge of Mr. Xu Zexiang and Mr. Zhu Ruoxi, the number of students has reached more than 150. The development of the school is quite impressive. Special attention is paid to the infusion of party ideas and extracurricular training. In order to promote the national pronunciation, the school held a Mandarin speech contest for all students in the Daxia Auditorium at 7 pm yesterday (the 29th), and invited Ms. Liu Shuzhao, Ms. Chen Shijian, Mr. Yang Bingyan, Mr. Liu Ziquan, and others to be judges. More than 100 people attended. After Principal Xu Zexiang presided over the ceremony, the speech began. The workers and students in the class had sharp diction, which was really unexpected. The topics, such as hard work and workers' lives, were novel in meaning and especially rare in public schools. As a result, Wang Changhong, Tao Weide, Xin Zhihong, and others won prizes.

Overview of Geological Research in China

Ye Liangfu, Geological Researcher at the Academia Sinica (2) Practical Contributions

This item is not easy to explain in detail because many technical terms are needed, so I can only talk about it roughly.

Judging from the surveys and research of the past ten years or so, although China's land is large and there are many types of minerals, the quantity is really too small. Only coal and iron are relatively abundant, but there is not as much as foreigners have speculated. The reserves of coal are about 210,000 billion tons (217,626 billion tons), of which anthracite is 400 billion tons (43,593 billion tons), bituminous coal and sub-bituminous coal are 170,000 billion tons (173,465 billion tons), lignite is 500 billion tons (568 billion tons), and it ranks fourth in the world compared with the world and the country (after the United States and Canada, Germany, and the United Kingdom). It is considered the first in the Far East. Important coalfields are of course in Zhili, Shandong, Henan, Shanxi, and the three northeastern provinces. There are 950 billion tons of iron ore. Important iron ore is in these provinces of Fengtian, Hebei, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangsu, Shandong, and Jiangxi. It ranks first among the Pacific Rim countries. If China's industry develops, it will only be enough for its own use for two or three hundred years.

In addition, there are only a few famous producing areas for antimony, tin, mercury, gold, tungsten, manganese, copper, zinc, and lead. It is still necessary to consider whether other scattered small mines can be utilized.

As for geological history, China is very complete from the oldest to the newest strata. The changes in land and sea and the changes in organisms in each era have been roughly understood. What is most lacking is the detailed geological structure of each province. This depends on someone's talent to do long-term work to understand.

In short, there are limited opportunities for the development of domestic industry and the need for specialized knowledge. Although there are results of work, few people use them, so the effectiveness of applying what you have learned is not obvious, which is a pity. Just in terms of mineral research, I dare say that the existing achievements and the degree of research seem to have exceeded what is needed domestically, but we are still moving forward, preparing materials for others to use.

There is also a kind of indirect contribution, that is, the spirit and achievements of the geological community in researching academics according to the track have actually aroused specialized talents in other sciences to also work. In recent years, domestic scientific research丨especially natural science丨has achieved some results. This is also one of the reasons.

(3) Research Talents

In the earliest period, there were only three or four geological talents in China who had returned from studying abroad. Subsequently, the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce of Beijing established the Geological Research Institute (Higher Vocational School). Three years later, it taught 22 people, two-thirds of whom served at the Beijing Geological Survey and most of them were sent abroad. Since then, Peking University has also run a geology department, and more than 100 people have graduated successively. There are also several people in various research institutions who have gone abroad to study. In addition, Central University, Sun Yat-sen University, Yenching University, and Shanxi University are mostly educating geological professionals there.

Finally, I want to say that there are several difficulties in studying geology in China. (1) There are too few leaders who can truly guide research. I am referring to leaders who are well-versed in research and have a wealth of knowledge, not leaders who are good at raising funds and socializing with all parties. Therefore, many people with aspirations to do research are mostly filling the role of pioneers and inevitably take detours to seek research success. In addition, it is difficult for the latecomers to gain much. Some people say that foreigners can be hired to guide this, although it is a way, but you must know that if you do not have considerable knowledge to control the foreigners, it is difficult for them to concentrate on guiding. Those who are really knowledgeable and willing to come to China also have their own purposes. (2) The funds for research institutions cannot be issued as planned, and those who do things cannot proceed boldly. (3) Now the local areas are too unstable and there are too many bandits, so it is impossible to calmly and smoothly go to the field for research. To improve future achievements, I can only hope that these difficulties will gradually decrease.

Discovery of a New Planet - Pluto

The new construction of the Nanjing Qintian Mountain Meteorological Observatory. According to records, 1500 years ago, the Song Dynasty established the Sun Observation Platform in Taicheng. In the Yuan Dynasty, during the Zhizheng period, the Meteorological Observatory was built here. In the Ming Dynasty, it was renamed the Qintian Observatory. In the early Qing Dynasty, it was moved to Beijing. The platform was destroyed by tides. Now, it has been restored to its former glory. Its origins are profound, and no modern observatory in the world can compare. To the right is Dr. Zhu Coching, the director of the Institute of Meteorology of the Academia Sinica.

We previously knew of eight planets, but now there is the discovery of a ninth planet. This new planet was located in Cancer on January 1st, and on January 21st of this year, it was near Gemini. It revolves around the sun like Uranus, Neptune, and Wang Man, forming a circle. This is the result of Dr. Tombaugh's mathematical research over sixteen years and represents a major advance in astronomy.

The Far East Meteorological Directors Conference was recently held in Hong Kong. From right to left: First, Shen Youqiao, the representative of the Dongsha Island Meteorological Observatory; second, a representative from [missing word] Meteorological Observatory; fourth, Shen Xiaoming, the representative of the Institute of Meteorology of the Academia Sinica. (X Wenhui)

The celestial image shown in the picture was taken by the Lowell Observatory on March 2nd using a 24-inch telescope. The arrowhead points to the true image of the new planet. It is 3.27 billion miles from Earth, with a volume similar to Earth but smaller than Jupiter, but this is still undetermined.
